<p>The <b>Democratic Republic of the Congo</b> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">République démocratique du Congo (RDC)</i> <small></small><span class="IPA" lang="fr-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[kɔ̃ɡo]</a></span>), informally <b>Congo-Kinshasa</b>, <b>DR Congo</b>, <b>the DRC</b>, <b>the DROC</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DROC_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-DROC-8">[7]</a></sup> or <b>the Congo</b>, and formerly and also colloquially <b><a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a></b>, is a country in <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a>. It is bordered to the northwest by the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a>, to the north by the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a>, to the northeast by <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, to the east by <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, and by <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a> (across <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a>), to the south and southeast by <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>, to the southwest by <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, and to the west by the South Atlantic Ocean and the <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_Province" title="Cabinda Province">Cabinda exclave of Angola</a>. By area, it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_countries_by_area" title="List of African countries by area">second-largest country in Africa</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">11th-largest in the world</a>. With a population of around 108 million, the Democratic Republic of the Congo is the most populous <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_territories_where_French_is_an_official_language" title="List of countries and territories where French is an official language">officially Francophone country</a> in the world. The <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a>, which is also the nation's economic center.
</p><p>Centered on the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Basin" title="Congo Basin">Congo Basin</a>, the territory of the DRC was first inhabited by Central African foragers around 90,000 years ago and was reached by the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu expansion</a> about 3,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup> In the west, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kingdom of Kongo</a> ruled around the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> from the 14th to 19th centuries. In the northeast, center and east, the kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Zande_people" title="Zande people">Azande</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Luba" title="Kingdom of Luba">Luba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Lunda" title="Kingdom of Lunda">Lunda</a> ruled from the 16th and 17th centuries to the 19th century. King <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II_of_Belgium" title="Leopold II of Belgium">Leopold II of Belgium</a> formally acquired rights to the Congo territory in 1885 and declared the land his private property, naming it the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a>. From 1885 to 1908, his <a href="/wiki/Force_Publique" title="Force Publique">colonial military</a> forced the local population to produce <a href="/wiki/Natural_rubber" title="Natural rubber">rubber</a> and committed <a href="/wiki/Atrocities_in_the_Congo_Free_State" title="Atrocities in the Congo Free State">widespread atrocities</a>. In 1908, Leopold <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II_of_Belgium#Relinquishment_of_the_Congo" title="Leopold II of Belgium">ceded</a> the territory, which thus became a <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian colony</a>.
</p><p>Congo achieved <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)">independence</a> from Belgium on 30 June 1960 and was immediately confronted by a series of <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis" title="Congo Crisis">seccessionist movements</a>, which culminated in the seizure of power of <a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">Mobutu</a> in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1965_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1965 Democratic Republic of the Congo coup d'état">1965 coup d'état</a>. Mobutu renamed the country <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a> in 1971 and imposed a harsh <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship" title="Dictatorship">dictatorship</a> until his overthrow in 1997 by the <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First Congo War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-3">[2]</a></sup> The country then had its name changed back and was confronted by the <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo War</a> from 1998 to 2003, which resulted in the deaths of 5.4 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRC2007fullreport_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-IRC2007fullreport-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_deadliest_war_in_the_world_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_deadliest_war_in_the_world-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRC2007Facts_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-IRC2007Facts-13">[12]</a></sup> The war ended under President <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kabila" title="Joseph Kabila">Joseph Kabila</a> who governed the country from 2001 to 2019, under whom <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Human rights in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">human rights in the country</a> remained poor and included frequent abuses such as <a href="/wiki/Enforced_disappearance" title="Enforced disappearance">forced disappearances</a>, torture, arbitrary imprisonment and restrictions on civil liberties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/2018_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_general_election" title="2018 Democratic Republic of the Congo general election">2018 general election</a>, in the country's first <a href="/wiki/Peaceful_transition_of_power" title="Peaceful transition of power">peaceful transition of power</a> since independence, Kabila was succeeded as president by <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi" title="Félix Tshisekedi">Félix Tshisekedi</a>, who has served as president since.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mwanamilongo_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mwanamilongo-15">[14]</a></sup> Since 2015, the Eastern DR Congo has been the site of an <a href="/wiki/Kivu_conflict" title="Kivu conflict">ongoing military conflict in Kivu</a>. 
</p><p>The Democratic Republic of the Congo is extremely rich in <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a> but has suffered from political instability, a lack of infrastructure, corruption, and centuries of both commercial and colonial extraction and exploitation, followed by more than 60 years of independence, with little widespread development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-:9-16">[15]</a></sup> Besides the capital Kinshasa, the two next largest cities, <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mbuji-Mayi" title="Mbuji-Mayi">Mbuji-Mayi</a>, are both mining communities. The DRC's largest export is raw minerals, with China accepting over 50% of its exports in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-3">[2]</a></sup> In 2019, DR Congo's level of human development was ranked 175th out of 189 countries by the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNHDR_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNHDR-17">[16]</a></sup> As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, following two decades of <a href="#Continental_and_civil_wars_(1996–2007)">various civil wars</a> and <a href="#Continued_conflicts_(2008–2018)">continued internal conflicts</a>, around 600,000 Congolese refugees were still living in neighbouring countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> Two million children risk starvation, and the fighting has displaced 4.5 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> The country is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_Market_for_Eastern_and_Southern_Africa" title="Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa">COMESA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_Central_African_States" title="Economic Community of Central African States">Economic Community of Central African States</a>.
</p>
