<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo people</a></div>
<p>The Democratic Republic of the Congo is named after the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a>, which flows throughout the country. The Congo River is the world's deepest river and the world's second-largest river <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_by_discharge" title="List of rivers by discharge">by discharge</a>. The <i>Comité d'études du haut Congo</i> ("Committee for the Study of the Upper Congo"), established by <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II_of_Belgium" title="Leopold II of Belgium">King Leopold II of Belgium</a> in 1876, and the <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_the_Congo" title="International Association of the Congo">International Association of the Congo</a>, established by him in 1879, were also named after the river.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Congo River was named by early European sailors after the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kingdom of Kongo</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> inhabitants, the <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo people</a>, when they encountered them in the 16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> The word <i>Kongo</i> comes from the <a href="/wiki/Kongo_language" title="Kongo language">Kongo language</a> (also called <i>Kikongo</i>). According to American writer Samuel Henry Nelson: "It is probable that the word 'Kongo' itself implies a public gathering and that it is based on the root <i>konga</i>, 'to gather' (trans[itive])."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> The modern name of the Kongo people, <i>Bakongo</i>, was introduced in the early 20th century.
</p><p>The Democratic Republic of the Congo has been known in the past as, in chronological order, the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian Congo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)">Republic of the Congo-Léopoldville</a>, the Democratic Republic of the Congo and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Zaire" title="Republic of Zaire">Republic of Zaire</a>, before returning to its current name the Democratic Republic of the Congo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-3">[2]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the time of independence, the country was named the Republic of the Congo-Léopoldville to distinguish it from its neighbour the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo-Brazzaville</a>. With the promulgation of the <a href="/wiki/Luluabourg_Constitution" title="Luluabourg Constitution">Luluabourg Constitution</a> on 1 August 1964, the country became the DRC but was renamed to <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a> (a past name for the Congo River) on 27 October 1971 by President <a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">Mobutu Sese Seko</a> as part of his <i><a href="/wiki/Authenticit%C3%A9_(Zaire)" title="Authenticité (Zaire)">Authenticité</a></i> initiative.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kisanganibobb_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-kisanganibobb-24">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>The word <i>Zaire</i> is from a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> adaptation of a Kikongo word <i>nzadi</i> ("river"), a truncation of <i>nzadi o nzere</i> ("river swallowing rivers").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> The river was known as <i>Zaire</i> during the 16th and 17th centuries; <i>Congo</i> seems to have replaced <i>Zaire</i> gradually in English usage during the 18th century, and <i>Congo</i> is the preferred English name in 19th-century literature, although references to <i>Zaire</i> as the name used by the natives (i.e. derived from Portuguese usage) remained common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1992, the Sovereign National Conference voted to change the name of the country to the "Democratic Republic of the Congo", but the change was not made.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> The country's name was later restored by President <a href="/wiki/Laurent-D%C3%A9sir%C3%A9_Kabila" title="Laurent-Désiré Kabila">Laurent-Désiré Kabila</a> when he overthrew Mobutu in 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> To distinguish it from the neighboring Republic of the Congo, it is sometimes referred to as <i>Congo (Kinshasa)</i> or <i>Congo-Kinshasa</i>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="History of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">History of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Congolese_history" title="Early Congolese history">Early Congolese history</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kingdom of Kongo</a></div>
<p>The geographical area now known as the Democratic Republic of the Congo was populated as early as 90,000 years ago, as shown by the 1988 discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Semliki_harpoon" title="Semliki harpoon">Semliki harpoon</a> at <a href="/wiki/Katanda_Territory" title="Katanda Territory">Katanda</a>, one of the oldest barbed harpoons ever found, believed to have been used to catch <a href="/wiki/Bagrus" title="Bagrus">giant river catfish</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a> reached <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a> at some point during the first millennium BC, then gradually started to expand southward. Their propagation was accelerated by the adoption of <a href="/wiki/Pastoralism" title="Pastoralism">pastoralism</a> and of <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> techniques. The people living in the south and southwest were foraging groups, whose technology involved only minimal use of metal technologies. The development of metal tools during this time period revolutionized agriculture. This led to the displacement of the hunter-gatherer groups in the east and southeast. The final wave of the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu expansion</a> was complete by the 10th century, followed by the establishment of the Bantu kingdoms, whose rising populations soon made possible intricate local, regional and foreign commercial networks that traded mostly in slaves, salt, iron and copper.
</p>
<h3><span id="Congo_Free_State_.281877.E2.80.931908.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Congo_Free_State_(1877–1908)">Congo Free State (1877–1908)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Congo Free State (1877–1908)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonisation_of_the_Congo" title="Colonisation of the Congo">Colonisation of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Atrocities_in_the_Congo_Free_State" title="Atrocities in the Congo Free State">Atrocities in the Congo Free State</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congo_Arab_war" title="Congo Arab war">Congo Arab war</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="947" data-file-width="1343" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg/220px-Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg/330px-Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg/440px-Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Leopoldville</a> Station and Port in 1884</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian exploration</a> and administration took place from the 1870s until the 1920s. It was first led by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Morton_Stanley" title="Henry Morton Stanley">Henry Morton Stanley</a>, who undertook his explorations under the sponsorship of King <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II_of_Belgium" title="Leopold II of Belgium">Leopold II of Belgium</a>. The eastern regions of the precolonial Congo were heavily disrupted by constant <a href="/wiki/Slave_raiding" title="Slave raiding">slave raiding</a>, mainly from Arab–Swahili <a href="/wiki/Arab_slave_trade" title="Arab slave trade">slave traders</a> such as the infamous <a href="/wiki/Tippu_Tip" title="Tippu Tip">Tippu Tip</a>, who was well known to Stanley.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>Leopold had designs on what was to become the Congo as a colony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cfskeyes_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-cfskeyes-34">[33]</a></sup> In a succession of negotiations, Leopold, professing humanitarian objectives in his capacity as chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Front_organization" title="Front organization">front organization</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_Internationale_Africaine" title="Association Internationale Africaine">Association Internationale Africaine</a></i>, actually played one European rival against another.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>King Leopold formally acquired rights to the Congo territory at the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference" title="Berlin Conference">Conference of Berlin</a> in 1885 and made the land his private property. He named it the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cfskeyes_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-cfskeyes-34">[33]</a></sup> Leopold's regime began various infrastructure projects, such as the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Matadi%E2%80%93Kinshasa_Railway" title="Matadi–Kinshasa Railway">railway that ran from the coast to the capital</a> of Leopoldville (now Kinshasa), which took eight years to complete.
</p><p>In the Free State, colonists coerced the local population into producing rubber, for which the spread of automobiles and development of rubber tires created a growing international market. Rubber sales made a fortune for Leopold, who built several buildings in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ostend" title="Ostend">Ostend</a> to honor himself and his country. To enforce the rubber quotas, the <i><a href="/wiki/Force_Publique" title="Force Publique">Force Publique</a></i> was called in and made the practice of cutting off the limbs of the natives a matter of policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google748_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-google748-35">[34]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the period of 1885–1908, millions of Congolese died as a consequence of exploitation and disease. In some areas the population declined dramatically – it has been estimated that <a href="/wiki/African_trypanosomiasis" title="African trypanosomiasis">sleeping sickness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> killed nearly half the population in the areas surrounding the lower Congo River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google748_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-google748-35">[34]</a></sup>
</p><p>News of the abuses began to circulate. In 1904, the British consul at Boma in the Congo, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Casement" title="Roger Casement">Roger Casement</a>, was instructed by the British government to investigate. His report, called the <a href="/wiki/Casement_Report" title="Casement Report">Casement Report</a>, confirmed the accusations of humanitarian abuses. The Belgian Parliament forced Leopold II to set up an independent commission of inquiry. Its findings confirmed Casement's report of abuses, concluding that the population of the Congo had been "reduced by half" during this period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-b1_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-b1-36">[35]</a></sup> Determining precisely how many people died is impossible, as no accurate records exist.
</p>
<h3><span id="Belgian_Congo_.281908.E2.80.931960.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Belgian_Congo_(1908–1960)">Belgian Congo (1908–1960)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Belgian Congo (1908–1960)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian Congo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bugidi,_the_mission_engineer,_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy,_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="760" data-file-width="464" decoding="async" height="278" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bugidi%2C_the_mission_engineer%2C_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy%2C_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg/170px-Bugidi%2C_the_mission_engineer%2C_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy%2C_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bugidi%2C_the_mission_engineer%2C_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy%2C_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg/255px-Bugidi%2C_the_mission_engineer%2C_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy%2C_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bugidi%2C_the_mission_engineer%2C_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy%2C_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg/340px-Bugidi%2C_the_mission_engineer%2C_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy%2C_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bugidi,_the_mission_engineer,_and_his_wife._Bakundi_was_a_Bateke_boy,_trained_by_Grenfell.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1908 photograph of a married <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a> couple.</div></div></div><p>
In 1908, the Belgian parliament, in spite of initial reluctance, bowed to international pressure (especially from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a>) and took over the Free State from King Leopold II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> On 18 October 1908, the Belgian parliament voted in favour of annexing the Congo as a Belgian colony. Executive power went to the <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_the_Colonies_(Belgium)" title="Minister of the Colonies (Belgium)">Belgian minister of colonial affairs</a>, assisted by a Colonial Council (Conseil Colonial) (both located in Brussels). The Belgian parliament exercised legislative authority over the Belgian Congo. In 1923 the colonial capital moved from Boma to Léopoldville, some 300 kilometres (190 mi) further upstream into the interior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica.com_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-38">[37]</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="974" data-file-width="972" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg/170px-Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg/255px-Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg/340px-Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Force_Publique" title="Force Publique">Force Publique</a></i> soldiers in the Belgian Congo in 1918. At its peak, the Force Publique had around 19,000 Congolese soldiers, led by 420 Belgian officers.</div></div></div><p>The transition from the Congo Free State to the Belgian Congo was a break, but it also featured a large degree of continuity. The last governor-general of the Congo Free State, Baron <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9ophile_Wahis" title="Théophile Wahis">Théophile Wahis</a>, remained in office in the Belgian Congo and the majority of Leopold II's administration with him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> Opening up the Congo and its natural and mineral riches to the Belgian economy remained the main motive for colonial expansion – however, other priorities, such as healthcare and basic education, slowly gained in importance.
</p><p>Colonial administrators ruled the territory and a dual legal system existed (a system of European courts and another one of indigenous courts, <i>tribunaux indigènes</i>). Indigenous courts had only limited powers and remained under the firm control of the colonial administration. The Belgian authorities permitted no political activity in the Congo whatsoever,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> and the <i>Force Publique</i> put down any attempts at rebellion.  
</p><p>The Belgian Congo was directly involved in the two world wars. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> (1914–1918), an initial stand-off between the <i>Force Publique</i> and the German colonial army in <a href="/wiki/German_East_Africa" title="German East Africa">German East Africa</a> turned into open warfare with a joint Anglo-Belgian-Portuguese invasion of German colonial territory in 1916 and 1917 during the <a href="/wiki/East_African_campaign_(World_War_I)" title="East African campaign (World War I)">East African campaign</a>. The <i>Force Publique</i> gained a notable victory when it marched into <a href="/wiki/Tabora" title="Tabora">Tabora</a> in September 1916 under the command of General <a href="/wiki/Charles_Tombeur" title="Charles Tombeur">Charles Tombeur</a> after heavy fighting. 
</p><p>After 1918, Belgium was rewarded for the participation of the <i>Force Publique</i> in the East African campaign with a <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> mandate over the previously German colony of <a href="/wiki/Ruanda-Urundi" title="Ruanda-Urundi">Ruanda-Urundi</a>. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the Belgian Congo provided a crucial source of income for the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_government_in_exile" title="Belgian government in exile">Belgian government in exile</a> in London, and the <i>Force Publique</i> again participated in <a href="/wiki/East_African_campaign_(World_War_II)" title="East African campaign (World War II)">Allied campaigns in Africa</a>. Belgian Congolese forces under the command of Belgian officers notably fought against the Italian colonial army in Ethiopia in <a href="/wiki/Asosa" title="Asosa">Asosa</a>, Bortaï<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Sa%C3%AFo" title="Siege of Saïo">Saïo</a> under Major-General <a href="/wiki/Auguste_Gilliaert" title="Auguste Gilliaert">Auguste-Eduard Gilliaert</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-WP-42">[41]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Independence_and_political_crisis_.281960.E2.80.931965.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_political_crisis_(1960–1965)">Independence and political crisis (1960–1965)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence and political crisis (1960–1965)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis" title="Congo Crisis">Congo Crisis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)">Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="343" data-file-width="293" decoding="async" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png/170px-Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png/255px-Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/82/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The leader of <a href="/wiki/ABAKO" title="ABAKO">ABAKO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu" title="Joseph Kasa-Vubu">Joseph Kasa-Vubu</a>, first democratically elected <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="President of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">President</a> of <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)">Congo-Léopoldville</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="424" data-file-width="467" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg/220px-Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg/330px-Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg/440px-Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba" title="Patrice Lumumba">Patrice Lumumba</a>, first democratically elected <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Prime Minister of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Prime Minister</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)">Congo-Léopoldville</a>, was murdered by Belgian-supported <a href="/wiki/State_of_Katanga" title="State of Katanga">Katangan separatists</a> in 1961</div></div></div>
<p>In May 1960, a growing nationalist movement, the <a href="/wiki/Mouvement_National_Congolais" title="Mouvement National Congolais">Mouvement National Congolais</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba" title="Patrice Lumumba">Patrice Lumumba</a>, won the <a href="/wiki/1960_Belgian_Congo_general_election" title="1960 Belgian Congo general election">parliamentary elections</a>. Lumumba became the first <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Prime Minister of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Prime Minister of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, then known as the Republic of the Congo, on 24 June 1960. The parliament elected <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu" title="Joseph Kasa-Vubu">Joseph Kasa-Vubu</a> as <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="President of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">president</a>, of the Alliance des Bakongo (<a href="/wiki/ABAKO" title="ABAKO">ABAKO</a>) party. Other parties that emerged included the <a href="/wiki/Parti_Solidaire_Africain" title="Parti Solidaire Africain">Parti Solidaire Africain</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Gizenga" title="Antoine Gizenga">Antoine Gizenga</a>, and the Parti National du Peuple led by Albert Delvaux and <a href="/wiki/Laurent_Mbariko" title="Laurent Mbariko">Laurent Mbariko</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Belgian Congo achieved independence on 30 June 1960 under the name "République du Congo" ("Republic of Congo" or "Republic of the Congo" in English). As the neighboring French colony of <a href="/wiki/French_Congo" title="French Congo">Middle Congo</a> (<i>Moyen Congo</i>) also chose the name "Republic of Congo" upon achieving its independence, the two countries are more commonly known as "Congo-Léopoldville" and "Congo-Brazzaville", after their capital cities.
</p><p>Shortly after independence the <i>Force Publique</i> mutinied, and on 11 July the <a href="/wiki/Katanga_Province" title="Katanga Province">province of Katanga</a> (led by <a href="/wiki/Mo%C3%AFse_Tshombe" title="Moïse Tshombe">Moïse Tshombe</a>) and <a href="/wiki/South_Kasai" title="South Kasai">South Kasai</a> <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis" title="Congo Crisis">engaged in secessionist struggles</a> against the new leadership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> Most of the 100,000 Europeans who had remained behind after independence fled the country,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> opening the way for Congolese to replace the European military and administrative elite.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> After the United Nations rejected Lumumba's call for help to put down the secessionist movements, Lumumba asked for assistance from the Soviet Union, who accepted and sent military supplies and advisers. On 23 August, the Congolese armed forces <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_South_Kasai" title="Invasion of South Kasai">invaded South Kasai</a>. Lumumba was dismissed from office on 5 September 1960 by Kasavubu who publicly blamed him for massacres by the armed forces in South Kasai and for involving Soviets in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> Lumumba declared Kasavubu's action unconstitutional, and a crisis between the two leaders developed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 September, Colonel <a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">Joseph Mobutu</a>, with the backing of the US and Belgium, removed Lumumba from office. On 17 January 1961, Lumumba was handed over to Katangan authorities and executed by Belgian-led Katangan troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> A 2001 investigation by Belgium's Parliament found Belgium "morally responsible" for the murder of Lumumba, and the country has since officially apologised for its role in his death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 18 September 1961, in ongoing negotiations of a cease-fire, a <a href="/wiki/1961_Ndola_United_Nations_DC-6_crash" title="1961 Ndola United Nations DC-6 crash">plane crash near Ndola</a> resulted in the death of <a href="/wiki/Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld" title="Dag Hammarskjöld">Dag Hammarskjöld</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General of the United Nations</a>, along with all 15 passengers, setting off a succession crisis. Amidst widespread confusion and chaos, a temporary government was led by technicians (the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Commissioners-General" title="College of Commissioners-General">Collège des commissaires généraux</a>). Katangan secession ended in January 1963 with the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Operation_in_the_Congo" title="United Nations Operation in the Congo">assistance of UN forces</a>. Several short-lived governments of <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Il%C3%A9o" title="Joseph Iléo">Joseph Ileo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyrille_Adoula" title="Cyrille Adoula">Cyrille Adoula</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mo%C3%AFse_Tshombe" title="Moïse Tshombe">Moise Kapenda Tshombe</a> took over in quick succession.
</p><p>Meanwhile, in the east of the country, Soviet and Cuban-backed rebels called the <a href="/wiki/Simba_rebellion" title="Simba rebellion">Simbas</a> rose up, taking a significant amount of territory and proclaiming a communist "People's Republic of the Congo" in Stanleyville. The Simbas were pushed out of Stanleyville in November 1964 during <a href="/wiki/Operation_Dragon_Rouge" title="Operation Dragon Rouge">Operation Dragon Rouge</a>, a military operation conducted by Belgian and American forces to rescue hundreds of hostages. Congolese government forces fully defeated the Simba rebels by November 1965.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lumumba had previously appointed Mobutu chief of staff of the new Congo army, <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Armed Forces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Armée Nationale Congolaise</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> Taking advantage of the leadership crisis between Kasavubu and Tshombe, Mobutu garnered enough support within the army to launch a coup. A <a href="/wiki/1964_Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)_constitutional_referendum" title="1964 Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville) constitutional referendum">constitutional referendum</a> the year before Mobutu's coup of 1965 resulted in the country's official name being changed to the "Democratic Republic of the Congo."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-3">[2]</a></sup> In 1971 Mobutu changed the name again, this time to "Republic of Zaire".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-54">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kisanganibobb_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-kisanganibobb-24">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Mobutu_dictatorship_and_Zaire_.281965.E2.80.931997.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobutu_dictatorship_and_Zaire_(1965–1997)">Mobutu dictatorship and Zaire (1965–1997)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Mobutu dictatorship and Zaire (1965–1997)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mobutu_Nixon.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="387" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mobutu_Nixon.gif/220px-Mobutu_Nixon.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mobutu_Nixon.gif/330px-Mobutu_Nixon.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mobutu_Nixon.gif/440px-Mobutu_Nixon.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mobutu_Nixon.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">Mobutu Sese Seko</a> and Richard Nixon in Washington, D.C., 1973.</div></div></div>
<p>Mobutu had the staunch support of the United States because of his <a href="/wiki/Anti-communism" title="Anti-communism">opposition to communism</a>; the U.S. believed that his administration would serve as an effective counter to communist movements in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">single-party system</a> was established, and Mobutu declared himself <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_state_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="List of heads of state of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">head of state</a>. He periodically held elections in which he was the only candidate. Although relative peace and stability were achieved, Mobutu's government was guilty of severe <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> violations, <a href="/wiki/Political_repression" title="Political repression">political repression</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Cult_of_personality" title="Cult of personality">cult of personality</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Corruption in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">corruption</a>.
</p><p>By late 1967 Mobutu had successfully neutralized his political opponents and rivals, either through co-opting them into his regime, arresting them, or rendering them otherwise politically impotent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201358_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201358-56">[55]</a></sup> Throughout the late 1960s, Mobutu continued to shuffle his governments and cycle officials in and out of the office to maintain control. Joseph Kasa-Vubu's death in April 1969 ensured that no person with First Republic credentials could challenge his rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201361–62_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201361–62-57">[56]</a></sup> By the early 1970s, Mobutu was attempting to assert Zaire as a leading African nation. He traveled frequently across the continent while the government became more vocal about African issues, particularly those relating to the southern region. Zaire established semi-clientelist relationships with several smaller African states, especially Burundi, Chad, and Togo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201364_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201364-58">[57]</a></sup>
</p><p>Corruption became so common the term "<i>le mal Zairois</i>" or "Zairian sickness",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> meaning gross corruption, theft and mismanagement, was coined, reportedly by Mobutu.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201374_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201374-60">[59]</a></sup> International aid, most often in the form of loans, enriched Mobutu while he allowed national infrastructure such as roads to deteriorate to as little as one-quarter of what had existed in 1960. Zaire became a <a href="/wiki/Kleptocracy" title="Kleptocracy">kleptocracy</a> as Mobutu and his associates embezzled government funds.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1664" data-file-width="1740" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg/220px-Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg/330px-Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg/440px-Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mobutu with the Dutch <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bernhard_of_Lippe-Biesterfeld" title="Bernhard of Lippe-Biesterfeld">Prince Bernhard</a> in Kinshasa in 1973</div></div></div>
<p>In a campaign to identify himself with African nationalism, starting on 1 June 1966, Mobutu renamed the nation's cities: Léopoldville became Kinshasa (the country was known as Congo-Kinshasa), Stanleyville became <a href="/wiki/Kisangani" title="Kisangani">Kisangani</a>, Elisabethville became <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a>, and Coquilhatville became <a href="/wiki/Mbandaka" title="Mbandaka">Mbandaka</a>. In 1971, Mobutu renamed the country the <i>Republic of Zaire</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kisanganibobb_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-kisanganibobb-24">[23]</a></sup> its fourth name change in eleven years and its sixth overall. The Congo River was renamed the Zaire River.
</p><p>During the 1970s and 1980s, Mobutu was invited to visit the United States on several occasions, meeting with U.S. Presidents <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> U.S. relations with Mobutu cooled, as he was no longer deemed necessary as a <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> ally. Opponents within Zaire stepped up demands for reform. This atmosphere contributed to Mobutu's declaring the Third Republic in 1990, whose constitution was supposed to pave the way for democratic reform. The reforms turned out to be largely cosmetic. Mobutu continued in power until armed forces forced him to flee in 1997. "From 1990 to 1993, the United States facilitated Mobutu's attempts to hijack political change", one academic wrote, and "also assisted the rebellion of Laurent-Desire Kabila that overthrew the Mobutu regime."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 1997, Mobutu died in exile in Morocco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Continental_and_civil_wars_.281996.E2.80.932007.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Continental_and_civil_wars_(1996–2007)">Continental and civil wars (1996–2007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Continental and civil wars (1996–2007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First Congo War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1444" data-file-width="1526" decoding="async" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png/220px-Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png/330px-Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png/440px-Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Belligerents of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo War</a></div></div></div>
<p>By 1996, following the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Civil_War" title="Rwandan Civil War">Rwandan Civil War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_genocide" title="Rwandan genocide">genocide</a> and the ascension of a <a href="/wiki/Tutsi" title="Tutsi">Tutsi</a>-led government in Rwanda, Rwandan <a href="/wiki/Hutu" title="Hutu">Hutu</a> militia forces (<a href="/wiki/Interahamwe" title="Interahamwe">Interahamwe</a>) fled to eastern Zaire and used refugee camps as bases for incursions against Rwanda. They allied with the Zairian Armed Forces to launch a campaign against Congolese ethnic Tutsis in eastern Zaire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>A coalition of Rwandan and Ugandan armies invaded Zaire to overthrow the government of Mobutu, launching the First Congo War. The coalition allied with some opposition figures, led by <a href="/wiki/Laurent-D%C3%A9sir%C3%A9_Kabila" title="Laurent-Désiré Kabila">Laurent-Désiré Kabila</a>, becoming the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Democratic_Forces_for_the_Liberation_of_Congo" title="Alliance of Democratic Forces for the Liberation of Congo">Alliance of Democratic Forces for the Liberation of Congo</a>. In 1997 Mobutu fled and Kabila marched into Kinshasa, naming himself as president and reverting the name of the country to the Democratic Republic of the Congo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kabila later requested that foreign military forces return to their own countries. Rwandan troops retreated to <a href="/wiki/Goma" title="Goma">Goma</a> and launched a new Tutsi-led rebel military movement called the <a href="/wiki/Rally_for_Congolese_Democracy" title="Rally for Congolese Democracy">Rassemblement Congolais pour la Democratie</a> to fight Kabila, while Uganda instigated the creation of a rebel movement called the <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_the_Congo" title="Movement for the Liberation of the Congo">Movement for the Liberation of the Congo</a>, led by Congolese warlord <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Bemba" title="Jean-Pierre Bemba">Jean-Pierre Bemba</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The two rebel movements, along with Rwandan and Ugandan troops, started the Second Congo War by attacking the DRC army in 1998. Angolan, Zimbabwean, and Namibian militaries entered the hostilities on the side of the government.
</p><p>Kabila was assassinated in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> His son <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kabila" title="Joseph Kabila">Joseph Kabila</a> succeeded him <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> and called for multilateral peace talks. UN peacekeepers, MONUC, now known as <a href="/wiki/MONUSCO" title="MONUSCO">MONUSCO</a>, arrived in April 2001. In 2002-03 Bemba intervened in the Central African Republic on behalf of its former president, <a href="/wiki/Ange-F%C3%A9lix_Patass%C3%A9" title="Ange-Félix Patassé">Ange-Félix Patassé</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> Talks led to a peace accord under which Kabila would share power with former rebels. By June 2003 all foreign armies except those of Rwanda had pulled out of Congo. A <a href="/wiki/Transitional_Government_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Transitional Government of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">transitional government</a> was set up until after the election. A constitution was approved by voters, and on 30 July 2006 DRC held its <a href="/wiki/2006_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_general_election" title="2006 Democratic Republic of the Congo general election">first multi-party elections</a>. These were the first free national elections since 1960, which many believed would mark the end to violence in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oxford_University_Press_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oxford_University_Press-70">[69]</a></sup> However, an election-result dispute between Kabila and Bemba turned into a skirmish between their supporters in Kinshasa. MONUC took control of the city. A new election took place in October 2006, which Kabila won, and in December 2006 he was sworn in as president.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg/220px-Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg/330px-Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg/440px-Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Refugees in the Congo</div></div></div>
<h3><span id="Continued_conflicts_.282008.E2.80.932018.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Continued_conflicts_(2008–2018)">Continued conflicts (2008–2018)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Continued conflicts (2008–2018)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kivu_conflict">Kivu conflict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Kivu conflict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kivu_conflict" title="Kivu conflict">Kivu conflict</a></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_(6988913212).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="833" data-file-width="1250" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg/220px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg/330px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg/440px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_(6988913212).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>People fleeing their villages due to fighting between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Military of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">FARDC</a> and rebel groups, <a href="/wiki/North_Kivu" title="North Kivu">North Kivu</a>, 2012</div></div></div><p><a href="/wiki/Laurent_Nkunda" title="Laurent Nkunda">Laurent Nkunda</a>, a member of <a href="/wiki/Rally_for_Congolese_Democracy%E2%80%93Goma" title="Rally for Congolese Democracy–Goma">Rally for Congolese Democracy–Goma</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Rally_for_Congolese_Democracy" title="Rally for Congolese Democracy">Rally for Congolese Democracy</a> branch integrated to the army, defected along with troops loyal to him and formed the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_for_the_Defence_of_the_People" title="National Congress for the Defence of the People">National Congress for the Defence of the People</a> (CNDP), which began an armed rebellion against the government. They were believed<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (May 2015)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> to be again backed by Rwanda as a way to tackle the Hutu group, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Forces_for_the_Liberation_of_Rwanda" title="Democratic Forces for the Liberation of Rwanda">Democratic Forces for the Liberation of Rwanda</a> (FDLR). In March 2009, after a deal between the DRC and Rwanda, Rwandan troops entered the DRC and arrested Nkunda and were allowed to pursue FDLR militants. The CNDP signed a peace treaty with the government in which it agreed to become a political party and to have its soldiers integrated into the national army in exchange for the release of its imprisoned members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> In 2012 <a href="/wiki/Bosco_Ntaganda" title="Bosco Ntaganda">Bosco Ntaganda</a>, the leader of the CNDP, and troops loyal to him, mutinied and formed the rebel military <a href="/wiki/March_23_Movement" title="March 23 Movement">March 23 Movement</a> (M23), claiming the government had violated the treaty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_(21_May_2013)_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._(8782972992).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg/220px-FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg/330px-FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg/440px-FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_(21_May_2013)_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._(8782972992).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Government troops near <a href="/wiki/Goma" title="Goma">Goma</a> during the <a href="/wiki/M23_rebellion" title="M23 rebellion">M23 rebellion</a> in May 2013</div></div></div>
<p>In the resulting <a href="/wiki/M23_rebellion" title="M23 rebellion">M23 rebellion</a>, M23 briefly captured the provincial capital of Goma in November 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> Neighboring countries, particularly Rwanda, have been accused of arming rebels groups and using them as proxies to gain control of the resource-rich country, an accusation they deny.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> In March 2013, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> authorized the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Force_Intervention_Brigade" title="United Nations Force Intervention Brigade">United Nations Force Intervention Brigade</a> to neutralize armed groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN1_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN1-77">[76]</a></sup> On 5 November 2013, M23 declared an end to its insurgency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup>
</p><p>Additionally, in northern <a href="/wiki/Katanga_Province" title="Katanga Province">Katanga</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mai-Mai" title="Mai-Mai">Mai-Mai</a> created by Laurent Kabila slipped out of the control of Kinshasa with <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A9d%C3%A9on_Kyungu" title="Gédéon Kyungu">Gédéon Kyungu Mutanga</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Mai-Mai_Kata_Katanga" title="Mai-Mai Kata Katanga">Mai Mai Kata Katanga</a> briefly invading the provincial capital of <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a> in 2013 and 400,000 persons displaced in the province as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> On and off fighting in the <a href="/wiki/Ituri_conflict" title="Ituri conflict">Ituri conflict</a> occurred between the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_and_Integrationist_Front" title="Nationalist and Integrationist Front">Nationalist and Integrationist Front</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Congolese_Patriots" title="Union of Congolese Patriots">Union of Congolese Patriots</a> who claimed to represent the <a href="/wiki/Lendu_language" title="Lendu language">Lendu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hema_people" title="Hema people">Hema</a> ethnic groups, respectively. In the northeast, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kony" title="Joseph Kony">Joseph Kony</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Resistance_Army" title="Lord's Resistance Army">Lord's Resistance Army</a> moved from their original bases in Uganda and South Sudan to DR Congo in 2005 and set up camps in the <a href="/wiki/Garamba_National_Park" title="Garamba National Park">Garamba National Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup>
</p><p>The war in the Congo has been described as the bloodiest war since World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-:9-16">[15]</a></sup> On 8 December 2017, fourteen UN soldiers and five Congolese regular soldiers were killed in a rebel attack at Semuliki in Beni territory. The rebels were thought to be <a href="/wiki/Allied_Democratic_Forces" title="Allied Democratic Forces">Allied Democratic Forces</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> UN investigations confirmed that aggressor in the December attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, <i>The New York Times</i> reported that people in the Congo continued to die at a rate of an estimated 45,000 per month<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> – estimates of the number who have died from the long conflict range from 900,000 to 5,400,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> The death toll is caused by widespread disease and famine; reports indicate that almost half of the individuals who have died are children under five years of age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> There have been frequent reports of weapon bearers killing civilians, of the destruction of property, of widespread sexual violence,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> causing hundreds of thousands of people to flee their homes, and of other breaches of humanitarian and human rights law. One study found that more than <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Sexual violence in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">400,000 women are raped</a> in the Democratic Republic of Congo every year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> In 2018 and 2019, Congo reported the highest levels of sexual violence in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oxford_University_Press_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-Oxford_University_Press-70">[69]</a></sup> According to the Human Rights Watch and the New York University-based Congo Research Group, armed troops in DRC's eastern Kivu region have killed over 1,900 civilians and kidnapped at least 3,300 people since June 2017 to June 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Kabila.27s_term_in_office_and_multiple_anti-government_protests"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kabila's_term_in_office_and_multiple_anti-government_protests">Kabila's term in office and multiple anti-government protests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Kabila's term in office and multiple anti-government protests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2015, <a href="/wiki/19_January_2015_DRC_protests" title="19 January 2015 DRC protests">major protests</a> broke out across the country and protesters demanded that Kabila step down as president. The protests began after the passage of a law by the Congolese lower house that, if also passed by the Congolese upper house, would keep Kabila in power at least until a national census was conducted (a process which would likely take several years and therefore keep him in power past the planned 2016 elections, which he is constitutionally barred from participating in). This bill passed; however, it was gutted of the provision that would keep Kabila in power until a census took place. A census is supposed to take place, but it is no longer tied to when the elections take place. In 2015, elections were scheduled for late 2016 and a tenuous peace held in the Congo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_DRC_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_DRC-90">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 November 2016 Congolese foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Tshibanda" title="Raymond Tshibanda">Raymond Tshibanda</a> told the press no elections would be held in 2016, after 20 December, the end of president Kabila's term. In a conference in Madagascar, Tshibanda said that Kabila's government had "consulted election experts" from Congo, the United Nations and elsewhere, and that "it has been decided that the voter registration operation will end on July 31, 2017, and that election will take place in April 2018."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/December_2016_Congolese_protests" title="December 2016 Congolese protests">Protests broke out in the country on 20 December</a> when Kabila's term in office ended. Across the country, dozens of protesters were killed and hundreds were arrested.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Renewed_regional_violence">Renewed regional violence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Renewed regional violence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ituri_conflict" title="Ituri conflict">Ituri conflict</a></div>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Jan_Egeland" title="Jan Egeland">Jan Egeland</a>, presently Secretary-General of the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Refugee_Council" title="Norwegian Refugee Council">Norwegian Refugee Council</a>, the situation in the DRC became much worse in 2016 and 2017 and is a major moral and humanitarian challenge comparable to the wars in Syria and Yemen, which receive much more attention. Women and children are abused sexually and "abused in all possible manners". Besides the conflict in <a href="/wiki/North_Kivu" title="North Kivu">North Kivu</a>, violence increased in the <a href="/wiki/Kasa%C3%AF_region" title="Kasaï region">Kasai region</a>. The armed groups were after gold, diamonds, oil, and cobalt to line the pockets of rich men both in the region and internationally. There were also ethnic and cultural rivalries at play, as well as religious motives and the political crisis with postponed elections. Egeland says people believe the situation in the DRC is "stably bad" but in fact, it has become much, much worse. "The big wars of the Congo that were really on top of the agenda 15 years ago are back and worsening".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> Disruption in planting and harvesting caused by the conflict was estimated to escalate starvation in about two million children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup>
</p><p>Human Rights Watch said in 2017 that Kabila recruited former March 23 Movement fighters to put down country-wide protests over his refusal to step down from office at the end of his term. "M23 fighters patrolled the streets of Congo's main cities, firing on or arresting protesters or anyone else deemed to be a threat to the president," they said.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup>
</p><p>Fierce fighting has erupted in Masisi between government forces and a powerful local warlord, General Delta. The United Nations mission in the DRC is its largest and most expensive peacekeeping effort, but it shut down five UN bases near Masisi in 2017, after the U.S. led a push to cut costs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 10 May 2018, Congolese gynecologist <a href="/wiki/Denis_Mukwege" title="Denis Mukwege">Denis Mukwege</a> was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> for his effort to end <a href="/wiki/Wartime_sexual_violence" title="Wartime sexual violence">the use of sexual violence as a weapon of war and armed conflict</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_ethnic_conflict">2018 ethnic conflict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2018 ethnic conflict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2018_Yumbi_violence" title="2018 Yumbi violence">2018 Yumbi violence</a></div>
<p>A tribal conflict erupted on 16–17 December 2018 at <a href="/wiki/Yumbi" title="Yumbi">Yumbi</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mai-Ndombe_Province" title="Mai-Ndombe Province">Mai-Ndombe Province</a>. Nearly 900 Banunu people from four villages were slaughtered by members of the Batende community in a deep-rooted rivalry over monthly tribal duties, land, fields and water resources. Some 100 Banunus fled to Moniende island in the Congo River, and another 16,000 to <a href="/wiki/Makotimpoko_District" title="Makotimpoko District">Makotimpoko District</a> in Republic of Congo. Military-style tactics were employed in the bloodbath, and some assailants were clothed in army uniforms. Local authorities and elements within the security forces were suspected of lending them support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-afp1_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-afp1-96">[95]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2018_election_and_new_president_.282018.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_election_and_new_president_(2018–present)">2018 election and new president (2018–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2018 election and new president (2018–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1075" data-file-width="1723" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg/220px-F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg/330px-F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg/440px-F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi_%26_Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>DR Congo's President <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi" title="Félix Tshisekedi">Félix Tshisekedi</a> with neighbouring Congolese President <a href="/wiki/Denis_Sassou_Nguesso" title="Denis Sassou Nguesso">Denis Sassou Nguesso</a> in 2020; both wear <a href="/wiki/Face_masks_during_the_COVID-19_pandemic" title="Face masks during the COVID-19 pandemic">face masks</a> due to the ongoing <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>On 30 December 2018 a <a href="/wiki/2018_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_general_election" title="2018 Democratic Republic of the Congo general election">general election</a> was held. On 10 January 2019, the electoral commission announced opposition candidate <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi" title="Félix Tshisekedi">Félix Tshisekedi</a> as the winner of the presidential vote,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> and he was officially sworn in as president on 24 January.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inaug_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-inaug-98">[97]</a></sup> However, there were widespread suspicions that the results were rigged and that a deal had been made between Tshisekedi and Kabila. The Catholic Church said that the official results did not correspond to the information its election monitors had collected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> The government had also "delayed" the vote until March in some areas, citing the <a href="/wiki/Kivu_Ebola_epidemic" title="Kivu Ebola epidemic">Ebola outbreak in Kivu</a> as well as the ongoing military conflict. This was criticized as these regions are known as opposition strongholds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> In August 2019, six months after the inauguration of Félix Tshisekedi, a coalition government was announced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup>
</p><p>The political allies of Kabila maintained control of key ministries, the legislature, judiciary and security services. However, Tshisekedi succeeded in strengthening his hold on power. In a series of moves, he won over more legislators, gaining the support of almost 400 out of 500 members of the National Assembly. The pro-Kabila speakers of both houses of parliament were forced out. In April 2021, the <a href="/wiki/Lukonde_cabinet" title="Lukonde cabinet">new government</a> was formed without the supporters of Kabila.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%932020_measles_outbreak_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="2019–2020 measles outbreak in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">major measles outbreak</a> in the country left nearly 5,000 dead in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup> The Ebola outbreak ended in June 2020, which had caused 2,280 deaths over 2 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> Another, smaller <a href="/wiki/2018_%C3%89quateur_province_Ebola_outbreak" title="2018 Équateur province Ebola outbreak">Ebola outbreak in the Équateur Province</a> began in June 2020, ultimately causing 55 deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> The global <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> also <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="COVID-19 pandemic in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">reached the DRC</a> in March 2020, with a <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_vaccination_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="COVID-19 vaccination in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">vaccination campaign</a> beginning on 19 April 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_ambassadors_of_Italy_to_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="List of ambassadors of Italy to the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Italian ambassador</a> to the DRC, <a href="/wiki/Luca_Attanasio" title="Luca Attanasio">Luca Attanasio</a>, and his bodyguard were <a href="/wiki/Killing_of_Luca_Attanasio" title="Killing of Luca Attanasio">killed in North Kivu on 22 February 2021</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> On 22 April 2021, meetings between Kenyan President <a href="/wiki/Uhuru_Kenyatta" title="Uhuru Kenyatta">Uhuru Kenyatta</a> and the Tshisekedi resulted in new agreements increasing international trade and security (counterterrorism, immigration, cyber security, and customs) between the two countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> In February 2022, <a href="/wiki/2022_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_allegations" title="2022 Democratic Republic of the Congo coup d'état allegations">allegations of a coup d'état</a> in the country led to uncertainty,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> but the coup attempt failed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output
