<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cg-map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="326" decoding="async" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Cg-map.png/220px-Cg-map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b4/Cg-map.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cg-map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The map of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_COD_present.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="1360" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Koppen-Geiger_Map_COD_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_COD_present.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Koppen-Geiger_Map_COD_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_COD_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Koppen-Geiger_Map_COD_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_COD_present.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_COD_present.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Democratic Republic of the Congo map of Köppen climate classification</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Geography of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Geography of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Geology of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Geology of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<p>The DRC is located in central <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a>, bordered to the northwest by the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a>, to the north by the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a>, to the northeast by <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, to the east by <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, and by <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a> (across Lake Tanganyika), to the south and southeast by <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>, to the southwest by <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, and to the west by the South Atlantic Ocean and the <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_Province" title="Cabinda Province">Cabinda Province exclave of Angola</a>. The country lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/6th_parallel_north" title="6th parallel north">6°N</a> and <a href="/wiki/14th_parallel_south" title="14th parallel south">14°S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/12th_meridian_east" title="12th meridian east">12°E</a> and <a href="/wiki/32nd_meridian_east" title="32nd meridian east">32°E</a>. It straddles the Equator, with one-third to the north and two-thirds to the south. With an area of 2,345,408 square kilometres (905,567 sq mi), it is the second-largest country in Africa by area, after Algeria.
</p><p>As a result of its equatorial location, the DRC experiences high precipitation and has the highest frequency of thunderstorms in the world. The annual rainfall can total upwards of 2,000 millimetres (80 in) in some places, and the area sustains the <a href="/wiki/Congolian_rainforests" title="Congolian rainforests">Congo rainforest</a>, the second-largest rain forest in the world after the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a>. This massive expanse of lush jungle covers most of the vast, low-lying central <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">basin</a> of the river, which slopes toward the Atlantic Ocean in the west. This area is surrounded by <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateaus</a> merging into <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savannas</a> in the south and southwest, by mountainous terraces in the west, and dense <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grasslands</a> extending beyond the Congo River in the north. The glaciated <a href="/wiki/Rwenzori_Mountains" title="Rwenzori Mountains">Rwenzori Mountains</a> are found in the extreme eastern region.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rainforest_-_Ituri_(20874628148).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Rainforest_-_Ituri_%2820874628148%29.jpg/220px-Rainforest_-_Ituri_%2820874628148%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Rainforest_-_Ituri_%2820874628148%29.jpg/330px-Rainforest_-_Ituri_%2820874628148%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Rainforest_-_Ituri_%2820874628148%29.jpg/440px-Rainforest_-_Ituri_%2820874628148%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rainforest_-_Ituri_(20874628148).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ituri_Rainforest" title="Ituri Rainforest">Ituri Rainforest</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a> produced the Congo River system which dominates the region topographically along with the rainforest it flows through. The <a href="/wiki/Congo_Basin" title="Congo Basin">Congo Basin</a> occupies nearly the entire country and an area of nearly 1,000,000 km<sup>2</sup> (390,000 sq mi). The river and its tributaries form the backbone of Congolese economics and transportation. Major tributaries include the <a href="/wiki/Kasai_River" title="Kasai River">Kasai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sangha_River" title="Sangha River">Sangha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ubangi_River" title="Ubangi River">Ubangi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruzizi_River" title="Ruzizi River">Ruzizi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aruwimi_River" title="Aruwimi River">Aruwimi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lulonga_River" title="Lulonga River">Lulonga</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dem_congo_sat.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2261" data-file-width="2293" decoding="async" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Dem_congo_sat.jpg/220px-Dem_congo_sat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Dem_congo_sat.jpg/330px-Dem_congo_sat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Dem_congo_sat.jpg/440px-Dem_congo_sat.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dem_congo_sat.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satellite image of Democratic Republic of the Congo</div></div></div>
<p>The Congo River has the second-largest flow and the second-largest <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">watershed</a> of any river in the world (trailing the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon</a> in both respects). The sources of the Congo River are in the <a href="/wiki/Albertine_Rift" title="Albertine Rift">Albertine Rift</a> Mountains that flank the western branch of the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Rift" title="East African Rift">East African Rift</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Mweru" title="Lake Mweru">Lake Mweru</a>. The river flows generally west from Kisangani just below <a href="/wiki/Boyoma_Falls" title="Boyoma Falls">Boyoma Falls</a>, then gradually bends southwest, passing by <a href="/wiki/Mbandaka" title="Mbandaka">Mbandaka</a>, joining with the Ubangi River, and running into the <a href="/wiki/Pool_Malebo" title="Pool Malebo">Pool Malebo</a> (Stanley Pool). Kinshasa and <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a> are on opposite sides of the river at the Pool. Then the river narrows and falls through a number of cataracts in deep canyons, collectively known as the <a href="/wiki/Livingstone_Falls" title="Livingstone Falls">Livingstone Falls</a>, and runs past <a href="/wiki/Boma,_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Boma, Democratic Republic of the Congo">Boma</a> into the Atlantic Ocean. The river and a 37 kilometres (23 mi) wide strip of coastline on its north bank provide the country's only outlet to the Atlantic.
</p><p>The Albertine Rift plays a key role in shaping the Congo's geography. Not only is the northeastern section of the country much more mountainous, but tectonic movement results in <a href="/wiki/Volcanism" title="Volcanism">volcanic</a> activity, occasionally with loss of life. The geologic activity in this area also created the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">African Great Lakes</a>, four of which lie on the Congo's eastern frontier: <a href="/wiki/Lake_Albert_(Africa)" title="Lake Albert (Africa)">Lake Albert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Kivu" title="Lake Kivu">Lake Kivu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Edward" title="Lake Edward">Lake Edward</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a>. 
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Rift_valley" title="Rift valley">rift valley</a> has exposed an enormous amount of mineral wealth throughout the south and east of the Congo, making it accessible to mining. <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">Cobalt</a>, copper, <a href="/wiki/Cadmium" title="Cadmium">cadmium</a>, industrial and gem-quality <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diamonds" title="Diamonds">diamonds</a>, gold, silver, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germanium" title="Germanium">germanium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radium" title="Radium">radium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a>, iron ore, and coal are all found in plentiful supply, especially in the Congo's southeastern Katanga region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:An_aerial_view_of_the_towering_volcanic_peak_of_Mt._Nyiragongo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1680" data-file-width="2928" decoding="async" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/An_aerial_view_of_the_towering_volcanic_peak_of_Mt._Nyiragongo.jpg/220px-An_aerial_view_of_the_towering_volcanic_peak_of_Mt._Nyiragongo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/An_aerial_view_of_the_towering_volcanic_peak_of_Mt._Nyiragongo.jpg/330px-An_aerial_view_of_the_towering_volcanic_peak_of_Mt._Nyiragongo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/An_aerial_view_of_the_towering_volcanic_peak_of_Mt._Nyiragongo.jpg/440px-An_aerial_view_of_the_towering_volcanic_peak_of_Mt._Nyiragongo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:An_aerial_view_of_the_towering_volcanic_peak_of_Mt._Nyiragongo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mount_Nyiragongo" title="Mount Nyiragongo">Mount Nyiragongo</a>, which last erupted in 2021.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_rivi%C3%A8re_Lulilaka,_parc_national_de_Salonga,_2005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="344" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/La_rivi%C3%A8re_Lulilaka%2C_parc_national_de_Salonga%2C_2005.jpg/220px-La_rivi%C3%A8re_Lulilaka%2C_parc_national_de_Salonga%2C_2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/La_rivi%C3%A8re_Lulilaka%2C_parc_national_de_Salonga%2C_2005.jpg/330px-La_rivi%C3%A8re_Lulilaka%2C_parc_national_de_Salonga%2C_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/La_rivi%C3%A8re_Lulilaka%2C_parc_national_de_Salonga%2C_2005.jpg/440px-La_rivi%C3%A8re_Lulilaka%2C_parc_national_de_Salonga%2C_2005.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_rivi%C3%A8re_Lulilaka,_parc_national_de_Salonga,_2005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Salonga_National_Park" title="Salonga National Park">Salonga National Park</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paysage_du_territoire_de_Masisi_(28130228449).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1037" data-file-width="1383" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Paysage_du_territoire_de_Masisi_%2828130228449%29.jpg/220px-Paysage_du_territoire_de_Masisi_%2828130228449%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Paysage_du_territoire_de_Masisi_%2828130228449%29.jpg/330px-Paysage_du_territoire_de_Masisi_%2828130228449%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Paysage_du_territoire_de_Masisi_%2828130228449%29.jpg/440px-Paysage_du_territoire_de_Masisi_%2828130228449%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paysage_du_territoire_de_Masisi_(28130228449).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Masisi_Territory" title="Masisi Territory">Masisi Territory</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nord-Kivu,_RD_Congo_-_Vue_sur_un_crat%C3%A8re_aux_abords_de_la_ville_de_Goma._(22722760943).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Nord-Kivu%2C_RD_Congo_-_Vue_sur_un_crat%C3%A8re_aux_abords_de_la_ville_de_Goma._%2822722760943%29.jpg/220px-Nord-Kivu%2C_RD_Congo_-_Vue_sur_un_crat%C3%A8re_aux_abords_de_la_ville_de_Goma._%2822722760943%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Nord-Kivu%2C_RD_Congo_-_Vue_sur_un_crat%C3%A8re_aux_abords_de_la_ville_de_Goma._%2822722760943%29.jpg/330px-Nord-Kivu%2C_RD_Congo_-_Vue_sur_un_crat%C3%A8re_aux_abords_de_la_ville_de_Goma._%2822722760943%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Nord-Kivu%2C_RD_Congo_-_Vue_sur_un_crat%C3%A8re_aux_abords_de_la_ville_de_Goma._%2822722760943%29.jpg/440px-Nord-Kivu%2C_RD_Congo_-_Vue_sur_un_crat%C3%A8re_aux_abords_de_la_ville_de_Goma._%2822722760943%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nord-Kivu,_RD_Congo_-_Vue_sur_un_crat%C3%A8re_aux_abords_de_la_ville_de_Goma._(22722760943).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lake_Kivu" title="Lake Kivu">Lake Kivu</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Kivu" title="North Kivu">North Kivu</a> province</div></div></div>
<p>On 17 January 2002 <a href="/wiki/Mount_Nyiragongo" title="Mount Nyiragongo">Mount Nyiragongo</a> erupted, with the lava running out at 64 km/h (40 mph) and 46 m (50 yd) wide. One of the three streams of extremely fluid lava flowed through Goma, killing 45 and leaving 120,000 homeless. Four hundred thousand people were evacuated from the city during the eruption. The lava poisoned the water of Lake Kivu, killing fish. Only two planes left the local airport because of the possibility of the explosion of stored petrol. The lava passed the airport, ruining a runway and trapping several airplanes. Six months after the eruption, nearby <a href="/wiki/Nyamuragira" title="Nyamuragira">Mount Nyamuragira</a> also erupted. Mount Nyamuragira then erupted in 2006 and again in January 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity_and_conservation">Biodiversity and conservation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Biodiversity and conservation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Wildlife of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Wildlife of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Institut_Congolais_pour_la_Conservation_de_la_Nature" title="Institut Congolais pour la Conservation de la Nature">Institut Congolais pour la Conservation de la Nature</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Environmental issues in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Environmental issues in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_ecoregions_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="List of ecoregions in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">List of ecoregions in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bas-congo.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Bas-congo.JPG/220px-Bas-congo.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Bas-congo.JPG/330px-Bas-congo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Bas-congo.JPG/440px-Bas-congo.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bas-congo.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bas-Congo" title="Bas-Congo">Bas-Congo</a> landscape</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Okapi2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1482" data-file-width="1707" decoding="async" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Okapi2.jpg/220px-Okapi2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Okapi2.jpg/330px-Okapi2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Okapi2.jpg/440px-Okapi2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Okapi2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Okapi</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2488" data-file-width="2228" decoding="async" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg/220px-Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg/330px-Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg/440px-Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A male <a href="/wiki/Western_gorilla" title="Western gorilla">western gorilla</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hippo_pod_edit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="2160" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Hippo_pod_edit.jpg/220px-Hippo_pod_edit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Hippo_pod_edit.jpg/330px-Hippo_pod_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Hippo_pod_edit.jpg/440px-Hippo_pod_edit.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hippo_pod_edit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hippopotami" title="Hippopotami">Hippopotami</a></div></div></div>
<p>The rainforests of the Democratic Republic of the Congo contain great <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>, including many rare and <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> species, such as the common <a href="/wiki/Chimpanzee" title="Chimpanzee">chimpanzee</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bonobo" title="Bonobo">bonobo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_forest_elephant" title="African forest elephant">African forest elephant</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_gorilla" title="Mountain gorilla">mountain gorilla</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Okapi" title="Okapi">okapi</a> and the <a href="/wiki/White_rhinoceros" title="White rhinoceros">white rhinoceros</a>. Five of the country's national parks are listed as <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Garamba_National_Park" title="Garamba National Park">Garumba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kahuzi-Bi%C3%A9ga_National_Park" title="Kahuzi-Biéga National Park">Kahuzi-Biega</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salonga_National_Park" title="Salonga National Park">Salonga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virunga_National_Park" title="Virunga National Park">Virunga National Parks</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Okapi_Wildlife_Reserve" title="Okapi Wildlife Reserve">Okapi Wildlife Reserve</a>. The Democratic Republic of the Congo is one of 17 <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">Megadiverse countries</a> and is the most biodiverse African country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup>
</p><p>Conservationists have particularly worried about <a href="/wiki/Primate" title="Primate">primates</a>. The Congo is inhabited by several <a href="/wiki/Hominidae" title="Hominidae">great ape</a> species: the common chimpanzee (<i>Pan troglodytes</i>), the bonobo (<i>Pan paniscus</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_gorilla" title="Eastern gorilla">eastern gorilla</a> (<i>Gorilla beringei</i>), and possibly the <a href="/wiki/Western_gorilla" title="Western gorilla">western gorilla</a> (<i>Gorilla gorilla</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> It is the only country in the world in which bonobos are found in the wild. Much concern has been raised about great ape extinction. Because of hunting and habitat destruction, the chimpanzee, the bonobo and the gorilla, each of whose populations once numbered in the millions, have now dwindled down to only about 200,000 gorillas, 100,000 chimpanzees and possibly only about 10,000 bonobos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gorillas_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-gorillas-119">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chimpanzees_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-chimpanzees-120">[119]</a></sup> The gorillas, chimpanzee, bonobo, and okapi are all classified as <a href="/wiki/Conservation_status" title="Conservation status">endangered</a> by the <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature" title="International Union for Conservation of Nature">World Conservation Union</a>.
</p><p>Major environmental issues in DRC include deforestation, poaching, which threatens wildlife populations, water pollution and mining. 
</p><p>Displaced refugees cause or are otherwise responsible for significant deforestation, soil erosion and wildlife poaching. Another significant issue is environmental damage from the mining of minerals, especially diamonds, gold, and <a href="/wiki/Coltan" title="Coltan">coltan</a> – a mineral used to manufacture capacitors.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Provinces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Provinces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Territories of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Territories of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Administrative divisions of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Administrative divisions of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<p>The country is currently divided into the city-province of Kinshasa and 25 other <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Provinces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">provinces</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-3">[2]</a></sup> The provinces are subdivided into 145 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Territories of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">territories</a> and 32 cities. Before 2015, the country had 11 provinces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Politics of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Politics of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_kabila.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1973" data-file-width="1615" decoding="async" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Joseph_kabila.jpg/170px-Joseph_kabila.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Joseph_kabila.jpg/255px-Joseph_kabila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Joseph_kabila.jpg/340px-Joseph_kabila.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_kabila.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kabila" title="Joseph Kabila">Joseph Kabila</a> was President of the Democratic Republic of the Congo from January 2001 to January 2019.</div></div></div>
<p>After a four-year interlude between two constitutions, with new political institutions established at the various levels of government, as well as new administrative divisions for the provinces throughout the country, a new constitution came into effect in 2006 and politics in the Democratic Republic of the Congo finally settled into a stable <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Democratic_republic" title="Democratic republic">democratic republic</a>.
The 2003 transitional constitution<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> had established a parliament with a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> legislature, consisting of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Senate_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Senate of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Senate</a> and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="National Assembly of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">National Assembly</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Senate_(Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo)" title="Senate (Democratic Republic of the Congo)">Senate</a> had, among other things, the charge of drafting the new constitution of the country. The executive branch was vested in a 60-member cabinet, headed by a <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="President of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">President</a> and four vice presidents. The President was also the Commander-in-Chief of the armed forces. The transitional constitution also established a relatively independent judiciary, headed by a Supreme Court with constitutional interpretation powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2006 constitution, also known as the Constitution of the Third Republic, came into effect in February 2006. It had concurrent authority, however, with the transitional constitution until the inauguration of the elected officials who emerged from the July 2006 elections. Under the new constitution, the legislature remained bicameral; the executive was concomitantly undertaken by a President and the government, led by a Prime Minister, appointed from the party able to secure a majority in the National Assembly.
</p><p>The government – not the President – is responsible to the Parliament. The new constitution also granted new powers to the provincial governments, creating provincial parliaments which have oversight of the Governor and the head of the provincial government, whom they elect. The new constitution also saw the disappearance of the Supreme Court, which was divided into three new institutions. The constitutional interpretation prerogative of the Supreme Court is now held by the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Constitutional Court of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Constitutional Court</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although located in the Central African <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_geoscheme" title="United Nations geoscheme">UN subregion</a>, the nation is also economically and regionally affiliated with Southern Africa as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Foreign relations of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Foreign relations of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2640" data-file-width="3960" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg/220px-Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg/330px-Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg/440px-Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kabila" title="Joseph Kabila">Joseph Kabila</a> with U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in August 2014</div></div></div>
<p>The global growth in demand for scarce raw materials and the industrial surges in China, India, Russia, Brazil and other <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a> require that <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed countries</a> employ new, integrated and responsive strategies for identifying and ensuring, on a continual basis, an adequate supply of strategic and critical materials required for their security needs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-:8-126">[125]</a></sup> Highlighting the DR Congo's importance to United States national security, the effort to establish an elite Congolese unit is the latest push by the U.S. to professionalize armed forces in this strategically important region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are economic and strategic incentives to bring more security to the Congo, which is rich in natural resources such as <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a>, a strategic and critical metal used in many industrial and military applications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-:8-126">[125]</a></sup> The largest use of cobalt is in <a href="/wiki/Superalloy" title="Superalloy">superalloys</a>, used to make <a href="/wiki/Jet_engine" title="Jet engine">jet engine</a> parts. Cobalt is also used in <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_alloy" title="Magnetic alloy">magnetic alloys</a> and in cutting and wear-resistant materials such as cemented <a href="/wiki/Carbide" title="Carbide">carbides</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemical industry</a> consumes significant quantities of cobalt in a variety of applications including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catalyst" title="Catalyst">catalysts</a> for petroleum and chemical processing; drying agents for paints and inks; ground coats for porcelain enamels; decolorant for ceramics and glass; and pigments for ceramics, paints, and plastics. The country possesses 80% of the world's cobalt reserves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup>
</p><p>It is thought that due to the importance of cobalt for batteries for electric vehicles and stabilization of electric grids with large proportions of intermittent renewables in the electricity mix, the DRC could become an object of increased geopolitical competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_126-2"><a href="#cite_note-:8-126">[125]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 21st century, <a href="/wiki/China%E2%80%93Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_relations#Present_economic_relations" title="China–Democratic Republic of the Congo relations">Chinese investment</a> in the DRC and Congolese exports to China have grown rapidly. In July 2019, UN ambassadors of 37 countries, including DRC, have signed a joint letter to the UNHRC defending China's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xinjiang_re-education_camps" title="Xinjiang re-education camps">treatment of Uyghurs</a> and other Muslim ethnic minorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> In 2021, President <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi" title="Félix Tshisekedi">Félix Tshisekedi</a> called for a review of mining contracts signed with <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> by his predecessor <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kabila" title="Joseph Kabila">Joseph Kabila</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> in particular the Sicomines multibillion <a href="/wiki/China%E2%80%93Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_relations#Sicomines" title="China–Democratic Republic of the Congo relations">'minerals-for-infrastructure' deal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Armed Forces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Armed Forces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aveba,_district_de_l%E2%80%99Ituri,_Province_Orientale,_DR_Congo_-_Des_militaires_FARDC_en_patrouille._(16643921095).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Aveba%2C_district_de_l%E2%80%99Ituri%2C_Province_Orientale%2C_DR_Congo_-_Des_militaires_FARDC_en_patrouille._%2816643921095%29.jpg/300px-Aveba%2C_district_de_l%E2%80%99Ituri%2C_Province_Orientale%2C_DR_Congo_-_Des_militaires_FARDC_en_patrouille._%2816643921095%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Aveba%2C_district_de_l%E2%80%99Ituri%2C_Province_Orientale%2C_DR_Congo_-_Des_militaires_FARDC_en_patrouille._%2816643921095%29.jpg/450px-Aveba%2C_district_de_l%E2%80%99Ituri%2C_Province_Orientale%2C_DR_Congo_-_Des_militaires_FARDC_en_patrouille._%2816643921095%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Aveba%2C_district_de_l%E2%80%99Ituri%2C_Province_Orientale%2C_DR_Congo_-_Des_militaires_FARDC_en_patrouille._%2816643921095%29.jpg/600px-Aveba%2C_district_de_l%E2%80%99Ituri%2C_Province_Orientale%2C_DR_Congo_-_Des_militaires_FARDC_en_patrouille._%2816643921095%29.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aveba,_district_de_l%E2%80%99Ituri,_Province_Orientale,_DR_Congo_-_Des_militaires_FARDC_en_patrouille._(16643921095).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>FARDC soldiers on patrol in Ituri province</div></div></div>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Armed Forces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Forces Armées de la République Démocratique du Congo</a></i> (FARDC) consist of about 144,000 personnel, the majority of whom are part of the <a href="/wiki/Land_Forces_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Land Forces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">land forces</a>, also with a small <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Air Force of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">air force</a> and an even smaller <a href="/wiki/Navy_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Navy of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">navy</a>. The FARDC was established in 2003 after the end of the Second Congo War and integrated many former rebel groups into its ranks. Due to the presence of undisciplined and poorly trained ex-rebels, as well as a lack of funding and having spent years fighting against different militias, the FARDC suffers from rampant corruption and inefficiency. The agreements signed at the end of the Second Congo War called for a new "national, restructured and integrated" army that would be made up of Kabila's government forces (the FAC), the RCD, and the MLC. Also stipulated was that rebels like the RCD-N, RCD-ML, and the <a href="/wiki/Mai-Mai" title="Mai-Mai">Mai-Mai</a> would become part of the new armed forces. It also provided for the creation of a <i>Conseil Superieur de la Defense</i> (Superior Defence Council) which would declare states of siege or war and give advice on security sector reform, disarmament/demobilisation, and national defence policy. The FARDC is organised on the basis of brigades, which are dispersed throughout the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Provinces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">provinces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>. Congolese troops have been fighting the <a href="/wiki/Kivu_conflict" title="Kivu conflict">Kivu conflict</a> in the eastern <a href="/wiki/North_Kivu" title="North Kivu">North Kivu</a> region, the <a href="/wiki/Ituri_conflict" title="Ituri conflict">Ituri conflict</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Ituri_Province" title="Ituri Province">Ituri</a> region, and other rebellions since the Second Congo War. Besides the FARDC, the largest peacekeeping mission of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, known as <a href="/wiki/MONUSCO" title="MONUSCO">MONUSCO</a>, is also present in the country with about 18,000 peacekeepers.
</p><p>The Democratic Republic of Congo signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption">Corruption</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Corruption">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Corruption in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Corruption in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<p>A relative of Mobutu explained how the government illicitly collected revenue during his rule: "Mobutu would ask one of us to go to the bank and take out a million. We'd go to an intermediary and tell him to get five million. He would go to the bank with Mobutu's authority and take out ten. Mobutu got one, and we took the other nine."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-a_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-a-134">[133]</a></sup> Mobutu institutionalized corruption to prevent political rivals from challenging his control, leading to an <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo#1990s" title="Economy of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">economic collapse in 1996</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-b_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-b-135">[134]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mobutu allegedly stole as much as US$4–5 billion while in office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-c_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-c-136">[135]</a></sup> He was not the first corrupt Congolese leader by any means: "Government as a system of organized theft goes back to King Leopold II," noted <a href="/wiki/Adam_Hochschild" title="Adam Hochschild">Adam Hochschild</a> in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AH_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-AH-137">[136]</a></sup> In July 2009, a Swiss court determined that the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_limitations" title="Statute of limitations">statute of limitations</a> had run out on an <a href="/wiki/International_asset_recovery" title="International asset recovery">international asset recovery</a> case of about $6.7 million of deposits of Mobutu's in a Swiss bank, and therefore the assets should be returned to Mobutu's family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup>
</p><p>President Kabila established the Commission of Repression of Economic Crimes upon his ascension to power in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-d_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-d-139">[138]</a></sup> However, in 2016 the <a href="/wiki/Enough_Project" title="Enough Project">Enough Project</a> issued a report claiming that the Congo is run as a violent <a href="/wiki/Kleptocracy" title="Kleptocracy">kleptocracy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2020, a court in the Democratic Republic of Congo found President Tshisekedi's chief of staff <a href="/wiki/Vital_Kamerhe" title="Vital Kamerhe">Vital Kamerhe</a> guilty of corruption. He was sentenced to 20 years' hard labour, after facing charges of embezzling almost $50m (£39m) of public funds. He was the most high-profile figure to be convicted of corruption in the DRC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2021, a judicial investigation targeting Kabila and his associates was opened in Kinshasa after revelations of alleged embezzlement of $138 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1352" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg/220px-DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg/330px-DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg/440px-DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A group of demobilized <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Child_soldiers" title="Child soldiers">child soldiers</a> in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Human rights in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Human rights in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Sexual violence in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Sexual violence in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Child_soldiers_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Child soldiers in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Child soldiers in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court_investigation_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="International Criminal Court investigation in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">International Criminal Court investigation in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> was initiated by Kabila in April 2004. The International Criminal Court prosecutor opened the case in June 2004.<a href="/wiki/Children_in_the_military" title="Children in the military">Child soldiers</a> have been used on a large scale in DRC, and in 2011 it was estimated that 30,000 children were still operating with armed groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup> Instances of child labor and <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour" title="Forced labour">forced labor</a> have been observed and reported in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Labor" title="United States Department of Labor">U.S. Department of Labor</a>'s <i>Findings on the Worst Forms of Child Labor</i> in the DRC in 2013<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> and six goods produced by the country's mining industry appear on the department's December 2014 <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Goods_Produced_by_Child_Labor_or_Forced_Labor" title="List of Goods Produced by Child Labor or Forced Labor">List of Goods Produced by Child Labor or Forced Labor</a></i>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime_and_law_enforcement">Crime and law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Crime and law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Crime in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Crime in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Congolese_National_Police" title="Congolese National Police">Congolese National Police</a> are the primary police force in the Democratic Republic of the Congo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Violence_against_women">Violence against women</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Violence against women">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Sexual violence in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Sexual violence in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_macho-violence_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Military macho-violence in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Military macho-violence in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court_investigation_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="International Criminal Court investigation in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">International Criminal Court investigation in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Violence_against_women" title="Violence against women">Violence against women</a> seems to be perceived by large sectors of society to be normal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> The 2013–2014 <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">DHS survey</a> (pp. 299) found that 74.8% of women agreed that a husband is justified in beating his wife in certain circumstances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup>
</p><p>The United Nations <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Elimination_of_All_Forms_of_Discrimination_Against_Women" title="Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination Against Women">Committee on the Elimination of Discrimination against Women</a> in 2006 expressed concern that in the post-war transition period, the promotion of women's human rights and gender equality is not seen as a priority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> Mass rapes, sexual violence and sexual slavery are used as a weapon of war by the Armed Forces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo and armed groups in the eastern part of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> The eastern part of the country in particular has been described as the "rape capital of the world" and the prevalence of sexual violence there described as the worst in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-151">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">Female genital mutilation</a> (FGM) is also practiced in DRC, although not on a large scale. The prevalence of FGM is estimated at 5% of women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup> FGM is illegal: the law imposes a penalty of two to five years of prison and a fine of 200,000 Congolese francs on any person who violates the "physical or functional integrity" of the genital organs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2007, the International Committee of the Red Cross expressed concern about the situation in eastern DRC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> A phenomenon of "pendulum displacement" has developed, where people hasten at night to safety. According to Yakin Ertürk, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Special_Rapporteur" title="United Nations Special Rapporteur">UN Special Rapporteur</a> on Violence against Women who toured eastern Congo in July 2007, violence against women in North and South Kivu included "unimaginable brutality". Ertürk added that "Armed groups attack local communities, loot, rape, kidnap women and children, and make them work as sexual slaves".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> In December 2008, GuardianFilms of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> released a film documenting the testimony of over 400 women and girls who had been abused by marauding militia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2010, <a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a> reported a dramatic increase in the number of rapes in the Democratic Republic of the Congo, and researchers from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harvard" title="Harvard">Harvard</a> discovered that rapes committed by civilians had increased seventeenfold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup> In June 2014, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_from_Torture" title="Freedom from Torture">Freedom from Torture</a> published reported rape and sexual violence being used routinely by state officials in Congolese prisons as punishment for politically active women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freedomfromtorture.org_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-freedomfromtorture.org-161">[160]</a></sup> The women included in the report were abused in several locations across the country including the capital Kinshasa and other areas away from the conflict zones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freedomfromtorture.org_161-1"><a href="#cite_note-freedomfromtorture.org-161">[160]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, figures both inside and outside of the country, such as Filimbi and <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Weyi" title="Emmanuel Weyi">Emmanuel Weyi</a>, spoke out about the need to curb violence and instability as the 2016 elections approached.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Economy of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Economy of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Poverty in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Poverty in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_Product_Exports_(2019).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="715" data-file-width="1100" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/290px-Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/435px-Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/580px-Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_Product_Exports_(2019).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional representation of Democratic Republic of the Congo exports, 2019</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GDP_per_capita_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_Congo.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="850" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/GDP_per_capita_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_Congo.svg/220px-GDP_per_capita_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_Congo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/GDP_per_capita_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_Congo.svg/330px-GDP_per_capita_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_Congo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/GDP_per_capita_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_Congo.svg/440px-GDP_per_capita_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_Congo.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GDP_per_capita_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_Congo.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Change in per capita GDP of Congo, 1950–2018. Figures are inflation-adjusted to 2011 International dollars.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_the_Congo" title="Central Bank of the Congo">Central Bank of the Congo</a> is responsible for developing and maintaining the <a href="/wiki/Congolese_franc" title="Congolese franc">Congolese franc</a>, which serves as the primary form of currency in the Democratic Republic of the Congo. In 2007, The World Bank decided to grant the Democratic Republic of Congo up to $1.3 billion in assistance funds over the following three years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup> The Congolese government started negotiating membership in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (OHADA), in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ohada.com_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-ohada.com-165">[164]</a></sup>
</p><p>The DRC is widely considered one of the world's richest countries in natural resources; its untapped deposits of raw minerals are estimated to be worth in excess of US$24 trillion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup> The DRC has 70% of the world's coltan, a third of its cobalt, more than 30% of its diamond reserves, and a tenth of its copper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite such vast mineral wealth, the economy of the Democratic Republic of the Congo has declined drastically since the mid-1980s. The DRC generated up to 70% of its export revenue from minerals in the 1970s and 1980s and was particularly hit when resource prices deteriorated at that time. By 2005, 90% of the DRC's revenues derived from its minerals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ExenbergerHartmann2007_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-ExenbergerHartmann2007-171">[170]</a></sup> Congolese citizens are among the poorest people on Earth. DR Congo consistently has the lowest, or nearly the lowest, <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">nominal GDP per capita</a> in the world. The DRC is also one of the twenty lowest-ranked countries on the <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining">Mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Mining industry of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Mining industry of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diamonds-_Zaire,_(DR_Congo)_(8458935824).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="899" data-file-width="966" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Diamonds-_Zaire%2C_%28DR_Congo%29_%288458935824%29.jpg/220px-Diamonds-_Zaire%2C_%28DR_Congo%29_%288458935824%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Diamonds-_Zaire%2C_%28DR_Congo%29_%288458935824%29.jpg/330px-Diamonds-_Zaire%2C_%28DR_Congo%29_%288458935824%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Diamonds-_Zaire%2C_%28DR_Congo%29_%288458935824%29.jpg/440px-Diamonds-_Zaire%2C_%28DR_Congo%29_%288458935824%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diamonds-_Zaire,_(DR_Congo)_(8458935824).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rough diamonds ≈1 to 1.5 mm in size from DR Congo.</div></div></div>
<p>The DRC is the world's largest producer of cobalt ore, and a major producer of copper and diamonds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup> The latter come from <a href="/wiki/Kasa%C3%AF_Province" title="Kasaï Province">Kasai province</a> in the west. By far the largest mines in the DRC are located in southern <a href="/wiki/Katanga_Province" title="Katanga Province">Katanga province</a> and are highly mechanized, with a capacity of several million tons per year of copper and cobalt ore, and refining capability for metal ore. The DRC is the second-largest diamond-producing nation in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup> and artisanal and small-scale miners account for most of its production.
</p><p>At independence in 1960, DRC was the second-most industrialized country in Africa after South Africa; it boasted a thriving mining sector and a relatively productive agriculture sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup> Foreign businesses have curtailed operations because of uncertainty about the outcome of long-term conflicts, lack of infrastructure, and the difficult operating environment. The wars intensified the impact of such basic problems as an uncertain legal framework, corruption, inflation, and lack of openness in government economic policy and financial operations.
</p><p>Conditions improved in late 2002, when a large portion of the invading foreign troops withdrew. A number of <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> missions met with the government to help it develop a coherent economic plan, and President Kabila began implementing reforms. Much economic activity still lies outside the GDP data. Through 2011 the DRC had the lowest Human Development Index of the 187 ranked countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Democratic_Republic_of_Congo,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="256" data-file-width="441" decoding="async" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png/330px-Democratic_Republic_of_Congo%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/38/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png 1.5x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Democratic_Republic_of_Congo,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>DR Congo's <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> scores, 1970–2010.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1754" data-file-width="2063" decoding="async" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg/220px-Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg/330px-Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg/440px-Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Collecting firewood in <a href="/wiki/Basankusu" title="Basankusu">Basankusu</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The economy of DRC relies heavily on mining. However, the smaller-scale economic activity from <a href="/wiki/Artisanal_mining" title="Artisanal mining">artisanal mining</a> occurs in the <a href="/wiki/Informal_economy" title="Informal economy">informal sector</a> and is not reflected in GDP data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup> A third of the DRC's diamonds are believed to be smuggled out of the country, making it difficult to quantify diamond production levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kitco_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kitco-177">[176]</a></sup> In 2002, tin was discovered in the east of the country but to date has only been mined on a small scale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup> Smuggling of <a href="/wiki/Conflict_resource" title="Conflict resource">conflict minerals</a> such as coltan and <a href="/wiki/Cassiterite" title="Cassiterite">cassiterite</a>, ores of <a href="/wiki/Tantalum" title="Tantalum">tantalum</a> and tin, respectively, helped to fuel the war in the eastern Congo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Katanga_Mining" title="Katanga Mining">Katanga Mining Limited</a>, a Swiss-owned company, owns the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luilu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luilu (page does not exist)">Luilu</a> Metallurgical Plant, which has a capacity of 175,000 tonnes of copper and 8,000 tonnes of cobalt per year, making it the largest cobalt refinery in the world. After a major rehabilitation program, the company resumed copper production operations in December 2007 and cobalt production in May 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2013, anti-corruption NGOs revealed that Congolese tax authorities had failed to account for $88 million from the mining sector, despite booming production and positive industrial performance. The missing funds date from 2010 and tax bodies should have paid them into the central bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup> Later in 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Extractive_Industries_Transparency_Initiative" title="Extractive Industries Transparency Initiative">Extractive Industries Transparency Initiative</a> suspended the country's candidacy for membership due to insufficient reporting, monitoring and independent audits, but in July 2013 the country improved its accounting and transparency practices to the point where the EITI gave the country full membership.
</p><p>In February 2018, global asset management firm <a href="/wiki/AllianceBernstein" title="AllianceBernstein">AllianceBernstein</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup> defined the DRC as economically "the Saudi Arabia of the electric vehicle age," because of its cobalt resources, as essential to the <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery" title="Lithium-ion battery">lithium-ion batteries</a> that drive <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">electric vehicles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Transport in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Transport in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:First_train_in_Kindu,_DRC.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="412" data-file-width="450" decoding="async" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/First_train_in_Kindu%2C_DRC.jpg/220px-First_train_in_Kindu%2C_DRC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/First_train_in_Kindu%2C_DRC.jpg/330px-First_train_in_Kindu%2C_DRC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/First_train_in_Kindu%2C_DRC.jpg/440px-First_train_in_Kindu%2C_DRC.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:First_train_in_Kindu,_DRC.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Train from <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a> arriving in <a href="/wiki/Kindu" title="Kindu">Kindu</a> on a newly refurbished line.</div></div></div>
<p>Ground transport in the Democratic Republic of Congo has always been difficult. The terrain and climate of the Congo Basin present serious barriers to road and rail construction, and the distances are enormous across this vast country. The DRC has more navigable rivers and moves more passengers and goods by boat and ferry than any other country in Africa, but air transport remains the only effective means of moving goods and people between many places within the country, especially in rural areas. Chronic economic mismanagement, political corruption and internal conflicts have led to long-term under-investment of infrastructure.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Rail transport in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Rail transport in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Train_rdc.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="559" data-file-width="671" decoding="async" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Train_rdc.svg/280px-Train_rdc.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Train_rdc.svg/420px-Train_rdc.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Train_rdc.svg/560px-Train_rdc.svg.png 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Train_rdc.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of rail network</div></div></div>
<p>Rail transportation is provided by the Congo Railroad Company (<a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_nationale_des_chemins_de_fer_du_Congo" title="Société nationale des chemins de fer du Congo">Société nationale des chemins de fer du Congo</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_commerciale_des_transports_et_des_ports" title="Société commerciale des transports et des ports">Office National des Transports Congo</a> and the Office of the Uele Railways (Office des Chemins de fer des Ueles, CFU). Like much of the infrastructure in the Congo, the railways are poorly maintained, dirty, crowded and dangerous.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The DRC has fewer all-weather paved highways than any country of its population and size in Africa — a total of 2,250 km (1,400 mi), of which only 1,226 km (762 mi) is in good condition. To put this in perspective, the road distance across the country in any direction is more than 2,500 km (1,600 mi) (e.g. Matadi to Lubumbashi, 2,700 km (1,700 mi) by road). The figure of 2,250 km (1,400 mi) converts to 35 km (22 mi) of paved road per 1,000,000 of population. Comparative figures for Zambia and Botswana are 721 km (448 mi) and 3,427 km (2,129 mi) respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup>
</p><p>Three routes in the <a href="/wiki/Trans-African_Highway_network" title="Trans-African Highway network">Trans-African Highway network</a> pass through DR Congo:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Tripoli%E2%80%93Cape_Town_Highway" title="Tripoli–Cape Town Highway">Tripoli–Cape Town Highway</a>: this route crosses the western extremity of the country on National Road No. 1 between Kinshasa and <a href="/wiki/Matadi" title="Matadi">Matadi</a>, a distance of 285 km (177 mi) on one of the only paved sections in fair condition.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lagos%E2%80%93Mombasa_Highway" title="Lagos–Mombasa Highway">Lagos–Mombasa Highway</a>: the DR Congo is the main missing link in this east–west highway and requires a new road to be constructed before it can function.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Beira%E2%80%93Lobito_Highway" title="Beira–Lobito Highway">Beira–Lobito Highway</a>: this east–west highway crosses Katanga and requires re-construction over most of its length, being an earth track between the Angolan border and <a href="/wiki/Kolwezi" title="Kolwezi">Kolwezi</a>, a paved road in very poor condition between Kolwezi and <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a>, and a paved road in fair condition over the short distance to the Zambian border.</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The DRC has thousands of kilometres of <a href="/wiki/Navigability" title="Navigability">navigable</a> <a href="/wiki/Waterway" title="Waterway">waterways</a>. Traditionally water transport has been the dominant means of moving around in approximately two-thirds of the country.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As of June 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, DR Congo had one major national airline (<a href="/wiki/Congo_Airways" title="Congo Airways">Congo Airways</a>) that offered flights inside DR Congo.
