Congo Airways was based at <a href="/wiki/N%27djili_Airport" title="N'djili Airport">Kinshasa's international airport</a>. All air carriers certified by the DRC have been banned from European Union airports by the European Commission, because of inadequate safety standards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup>
</p><p>Several international airlines service Kinshasa's international airport and a few also offer international flights to <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi_International_Airport" title="Lubumbashi International Airport">Lubumbashi International Airport</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Energy in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Energy in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<p>Both coal and crude oil resources were mainly used domestically up to 2008. The DRC has the infrastructure for hydro-electricity from the Congo River at the <a href="/wiki/Inga_dams" title="Inga dams">Inga dams</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[185]</a></sup> The country also possesses 50% of Africa's forests and a river system that could provide hydro-electric power to the entire continent, according to a UN report on the country's strategic significance and its potential role as an economic power in central Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup>
</p><p>The generation and distribution of electricity are controlled by <a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_Nationale_d%27%C3%89lectricit%C3%A9" title="Société Nationale d'Électricité">Société nationale d'électricité</a>, but only 15% of the country has access to electricity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[187]</a></sup> The DRC is a member of three electrical power pools. These are Southern African Power Pool, East African Power Pool, and Central African Power Pool.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Renewable_energy">Renewable energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Renewable energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Renewable energy in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Renewable energy in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<p>Because of abundant sunlight, the potential for solar development is very high in the DRC. There are already about 836 solar power systems in the DRC, with a total power of 83 MW, located in <a href="/wiki/Province_of_%C3%89quateur" title="Province of Équateur">Équateur</a> (167), Katanga (159), Nord-Kivu (170), the two Kasaï provinces (170), and Bas-Congo (170). Also, the 148 Caritas network system has a total power of 6.31 MW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[188]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Demographics of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Demographics of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Poverty in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Poverty in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Child_marriage_in_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Child marriage in Democratic Republic of the Congo">Child marriage in Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_-_DR_Congo,_major_languages.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="679" data-file-width="729" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg/220px-Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg/330px-Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg/440px-Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_-_DR_Congo,_major_languages.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The four Bantu languages with elevated "national" status.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Languages of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Languages of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of the Democratic Republic of the Congo. It is culturally accepted as the <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i>, facilitating communication among the many different ethnic groups of the Congo. According to a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">OIF</a> report, 49 million Congolese people (51% of the population) could read and write in French.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup> A 2021 survey found that 74% of the population could speak French, making it the most widely spoken language in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lingala_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-lingala-191">[190]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Kinshasa, 67% of the population in 2014 could read and write French, and 68.5% could speak and understand it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup>
</p><p>Approximately 242 languages are spoken in the country, of which four have the status of national languages: <a href="/wiki/Kituba_language" title="Kituba language">Kituba</a> (Kikongo), <a href="/wiki/Lingala" title="Lingala">Lingala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luba-Kasai_language" title="Luba-Kasai language">Tshiluba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>. Although some limited number of people speak these as first languages, most of the population speak them as a second language, after the native language of their own ethnic group. Lingala was the official language of the <i>Force Publique</i> under Belgian colonial rule and remains to this day the predominant language of the armed forces. Since the recent rebellions, a good part of the army in the east also uses Swahili, where it competes to be the regional lingua franca.
</p><p>Under Belgian rule, the colonizers instituted teaching and use of the four national languages in primary schools, making it one of the few African nations to have had literacy in local languages during the European colonial period. This trend was reversed after independence, when French became the sole language of education at all levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lang_educ_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-lang_educ-193">[192]</a></sup> Since 1975, the four national languages have been reintroduced in the first two years of primary education, with French becoming the sole language of education from the third year onward, but in practice many primary schools in urban areas solely use French from the first year of school onward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lang_educ_193-1"><a href="#cite_note-lang_educ-193">[192]</a></sup>
Portuguese is taught in the Congolese schools as a foreign language. The lexical similarity and phonology with French makes Portuguese a relatively easy language for the people to learn. Most of the roughly 175,000 Portuguese speakers in the DRC are Angolan and Mozambican expatriates.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Over 200 ethnic groups populate the DRC, of which the majority are <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a>. Together, <a href="/wiki/Mongo_people" title="Mongo people">Mongo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luba_people" title="Luba people">Luba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo</a> peoples, <a href="/wiki/Mangbetu_people" title="Mangbetu people">Mangbetu</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Zande_people" title="Zande people">Azande</a> peoples constitute around 45% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gates2010p14_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gates2010p14-194">[193]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2021, the UN estimated the country's population to be 96 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-195">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2022_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2022-196">[195]</a></sup> a rapid increase from 39.1 million in 1992 despite the ongoing war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup> As many as 250 ethnic groups have been identified and named. The most numerous people are the Kongo, Luba, and Mongo. About 600,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congo_Pygmies" title="Congo Pygmies">Pygmies</a> are the aboriginal people of the DR Congo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[197]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Religion in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Religion in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lubumbashi_Cathedral.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Lubumbashi_Cathedral.jpg/220px-Lubumbashi_Cathedral.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Lubumbashi_Cathedral.jpg/330px-Lubumbashi_Cathedral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Lubumbashi_Cathedral.jpg/440px-Lubumbashi_Cathedral.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lubumbashi_Cathedral.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sts._Peter_and_Paul_Cathedral,_Lubumbashi" title="Sts. Peter and Paul Cathedral, Lubumbashi">The Sts. Peter and Paul Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2178" data-file-width="4096" decoding="async" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png/220px-Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png/330px-Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png/440px-Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Peace_Cathedral,_Bukavu" title="Our Lady of Peace Cathedral, Bukavu">Our Lady of Peace Cathedral</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bukavu" title="Bukavu">Bukavu</a></div></div></div>
<p>Christianity is the predominant religion of the DRC. A 2013-14 survey, conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">Demographic and Health Surveys</a> Program in 2013–2014 indicated that Christians constituted 93.7% of the population (with Catholics making up 29.7%, Protestants 26.8%, and other Christians 37.2%). A new Christian religious movement, <a href="/wiki/Kimbanguism" title="Kimbanguism">Kimbanguism</a>, had the adherence of 2.8%, while Muslims made up 1%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHS_2013-14_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-DHS_2013-14-199">[198]</a></sup> Other recent estimates have found Christianity the majority religion, followed by 95.8% of the population according to a 2010 <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religion_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-religion-200">[199]</a></sup> estimate, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a> reports this figure to be 95.9%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[200]</a></sup> The proportion of followers of Islam is variously estimated from 1%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[201]</a></sup> to 12% <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[202]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are about 35 million Catholics in the country<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_3-6"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-3">[2]</a></sup> with six <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archdiocese" title="Archdiocese">archdioceses</a> and 41 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dioceses" title="Dioceses">dioceses</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[203]</a></sup> The impact of the Catholic Church is difficult to overestimate. Schatzberg has called it the country's "only truly national institution apart from the state."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[204]</a></sup> Its schools have educated over 60% of the nation's primary school students and more than 40% of its secondary students. The church owns and manages an extensive network of hospitals, schools, and clinics, as well as many diocesan economic enterprises, including farms, ranches, stores, and artisans' shops.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Sixty-two Protestant denominations are federated under the umbrella of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Christ_in_the_Congo" title="Church of Christ in the Congo">Church of Christ in the Congo</a>. It is often simply referred to as <i>the Protestant Church</i>, since it covers most of the DRC Protestants. With more than 25 million members, it constitutes <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_largest_Protestant_denominations" title="List of the largest Protestant denominations">one of the largest Protestant bodies</a> in the world.
</p><p>Kimbanguism was seen as a threat to the colonial regime and was banned by the Belgians. Kimbanguism, officially "the church of Christ on Earth by the prophet Simon Kimbangu", has about three million members,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adherents_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-Adherents-206">[205]</a></sup> primarily among the Bakongo of <a href="/wiki/Kongo_Central" title="Kongo Central">Kongo Central</a> and Kinshasa.
</p><p>Islam has been present in the Democratic Republic of the Congo since the 18th century, when Arab traders from <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">East Africa</a> pushed into the interior for ivory- and slave-trading purposes. Today, Muslims constitute approximately 1% of the Congolese population according to the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>. The majority are <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> Muslims.
</p><p>The first members of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a> to live in the country came from Uganda in 1953. Four years later the first local administrative council was elected. In 1970 the National Spiritual Assembly (national administrative council) was first elected. Though the religion was banned in the 1970s and 1980s, due to misrepresentations of foreign governments, the ban was lifted by the end of the 1980s. In 2012 plans were announced to build a national <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_House_of_Worship" title="Baháʼí House of Worship">Baháʼí House of Worship</a> in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[206]</a></sup>
</p><p>Traditional religions embody such concepts as <a href="/wiki/Monotheism" title="Monotheism">monotheism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vitalism" title="Vitalism">vitalism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spirit_worship" title="Spirit worship">spirit</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancestor_worship" title="Ancestor worship">ancestor worship</a>, <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft" title="Witchcraft">witchcraft</a>, and sorcery and vary widely among ethnic groups. The syncretic sects often merge elements of Christianity with traditional beliefs and rituals and are not recognized by mainstream churches as part of Christianity. New variants of ancient beliefs have become widespread, led by US-inspired Pentecostal churches which have been in the forefront of witchcraft accusations, particularly against children and the elderly.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="What is the new belief? Witchcraft, or the accusations of witchcraft? (January 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[207]</a></sup> Children accused of witchcraft are sent away from homes and family, often to live on the street, which can lead to physical violence against these children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[208]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="What leads to violence? (January 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[209]</a></sup> There are charities supporting street children such as the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Children_Trust" title="Congo Children Trust">Congo Children Trust</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[210]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Congo_Children_Trust" title="Congo Children Trust">Congo Children Trust</a>'s flagship project is Kimbilio,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[211]</a></sup> which works to reunite street children in <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a>. The usual term for these children is <i>enfants sorciers</i> (child witches) or <i>enfants dits sorciers</i> (children accused of witchcraft). Non-denominational church organizations have been formed to capitalize on this belief by charging exorbitant fees for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exorcisms" title="Exorcisms">exorcisms</a>. Though recently outlawed, children have been subjected in these exorcisms to often-violent abuse at the hands of self-proclaimed prophets and priests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Education in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Education in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DRC_classroom.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1197" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/DRC_classroom.jpg/220px-DRC_classroom.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/DRC_classroom.jpg/330px-DRC_classroom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/DRC_classroom.jpg/440px-DRC_classroom.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DRC_classroom.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A classroom in the Democratic Republic of the Congo.</div></div></div>
<p>In 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate for the population between the ages of 15 and 49 was estimated to be 75.9% (88.1% male and 63.8% female) according to a <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">DHS</a> nationwide survey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup> The education system is governed by three government ministries: the <i>Ministère de l'Enseignement Primaire, Secondaire et Professionnel (MEPSP</i>), the <i>Ministère de l'Enseignement Supérieur et Universitaire (MESU)</i> and the <i>Ministère des Affaires Sociales (MAS)</i>. Primary education is not free nor compulsory,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> even though the Congolese constitution says it should be (Article 43 of the 2005 Congolese Constitution).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[214]</a></sup>
</p><p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo Wars</a> in the late 1990s—early 2000s, over 5.2 million children in the country did not receive any education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-216">[215]</a></sup> Since the end of the civil war, the situation has improved tremendously, with the number of children enrolled in primary schools rising from 5.5 million in 2002 to 16.8 million in 2018, and the number of children enrolled in secondary schools rising from 2.8 million in 2007 to 4.6 million in 2015 according to <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[216]</a></sup>
</p><p>Actual school attendance has also improved greatly in recent years, with primary school net attendance estimated to be 82.4% in 2014 (82.4% of children ages 6–11 attended school; 83.4% for boys, 80.6% for girls).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[217]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Health in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Health in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="HIV/AIDS in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">HIV/AIDS in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Life_expectancy_in_DR_Congo.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="850" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Life_expectancy_in_DR_Congo.svg/220px-Life_expectancy_in_DR_Congo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Life_expectancy_in_DR_Congo.svg/330px-Life_expectancy_in_DR_Congo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Life_expectancy_in_DR_Congo.svg/440px-Life_expectancy_in_DR_Congo.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Life_expectancy_in_DR_Congo.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Development of life expectancy in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="List of hospitals in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">hospitals in the DRC</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa_General_Hospital" title="Kinshasa General Hospital">General Hospital of Kinshasa</a>. The DRC has the world's second-highest rate of <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a> (after Chad). In April 2011, through aid from <a href="/wiki/GAVI" title="GAVI">Global Alliance for Vaccines</a>, a new vaccine to prevent <a href="/wiki/Streptococcus_pneumoniae" title="Streptococcus pneumoniae">pneumococcal disease</a> was introduced around Kinshasa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[218]</a></sup> In 2012, it was estimated that about 1.1% of adults aged 15–49 were living with <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[219]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">Malaria</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[220]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[221]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">yellow fever</a> are problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[222]</a></sup> In May 2019, the death toll from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Kivu_Ebola_epidemic" title="2018–19 Kivu Ebola epidemic">Ebola outbreak</a> in DRC surpassed 1,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[223]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Maternal_health" title="Maternal health">Maternal health</a> is poor in DRC. According to 2010 estimates, DRC has the 17th highest <a href="/wiki/Maternal_death" title="Maternal death">maternal mortality</a> rate in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[224]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>, 43.5% of children under five are <a href="/wiki/Stunted_growth" title="Stunted growth">stunted</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[225]</a></sup>
</p><p>United Nations emergency food relief agency warned that amid the escalating conflict and worsening situation following <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019" title="Coronavirus disease 2019">COVID-19</a> in the DRC, millions of lives were at risk as they could die of hunger. According to the data of the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a>, in 2020 four in ten people in Congo lacked food security and about 15.6 million were facing a potential hunger crisis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[226]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">Air pollution</a> levels in the Democratic Republic of the Congo (DRC) are very unhealthy. In 2020, annual average air pollution in the Democratic Republic of the Congo stood at 34.2 µg/m³, which is almost 6.8 times the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> PM2.5 guideline (5 µg/m³: set in September 2021).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uchicago1_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-uchicago1-228">[227]</a></sup> These pollution levels are estimated to reduce the <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> of an average citizen of the DRC by almost 2.9 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uchicago1_228-1"><a href="#cite_note-uchicago1-228">[227]</a></sup> Currently, the DRC does not have a national ambient air quality standard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[228]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities">Largest cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Largest cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Migration">Migration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Migration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_(7134901927).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1250" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg/220px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg/330px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg/440px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_(7134901927).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population fleeing their villages due to fighting between FARDC and rebels groups, Sake North Kivu 30 April 2012</div></div></div>
<p>Given the often unstable situation in the country and the condition of state structures, it is extremely difficult to obtain reliable migration data. However, evidence suggests that DRC continues to be a destination country for immigrants, in spite of recent declines in their numbers. Immigration is very diverse in nature; refugees and asylum-seekers – products of the numerous and violent conflicts in the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">Great Lakes Region</a> – constitute an important subset of the population. Additionally, the country's large mine operations attract migrant workers from Africa and beyond. There is also considerable migration for commercial activities from other African countries and the rest of the world, but these movements are not well studied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IOMProfile_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-IOMProfile-232">[231]</a></sup> Transit migration towards South Africa and Europe also plays a role.
</p><p>Immigration to the DRC has decreased steadily over the past two decades, most likely as a result of the armed violence that the country has experienced. According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Migration" title="International Organization for Migration">International Organization for Migration</a>, the number of immigrants in the DRC has fallen from just over one million in 1960, to 754,000 in 1990, to 480,000 in 2005, to an estimated 445,000 in 2010. Official figures are unavailable, partly due to the predominance of the <a href="/wiki/Informal_economy" title="Informal economy">informal economy</a> in the DRC. Data are also lacking on irregular immigrants, however given neighbouring countries' ethnic links to DRC nationals, irregular migration is assumed to be a significant phenomenon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IOMProfile_232-1"><a href="#cite_note-IOMProfile-232">[231]</a></sup>
</p><p>Figures for Congolese nationals abroad vary greatly depending on the source, from three to six million. This discrepancy is due to a lack of official, reliable data. Emigrants from the DRC are above all long-term emigrants, the majority of whom live in Africa and to a lesser extent in Europe; 79.7% and 15.3% respectively, according to estimated 2000 data. New destination countries include South Africa and various points en route to Europe. The DRC has produced a considerable number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Refugees" title="Refugees">refugees</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asylum-seekers" title="Asylum-seekers">asylum-seekers</a> located in the region and beyond. These numbers peaked in 2004 when, according to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNHCR" title="UNHCR">UNHCR</a>, there were more than 460,000 refugees from the DRC; in 2008, Congolese refugees numbered 367,995 in total, 68% of whom were living in other African countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IOMProfile_232-2"><a href="#cite_note-IOMProfile-232">[231]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2003, more than 400,000 Congolese migrants have been expelled from <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[232]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Culture of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Culture of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Congolese_cuisine" title="Congolese cuisine">Congolese cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hemba_male_figure1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="853" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Hemba_male_figure1.jpg/170px-Hemba_male_figure1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Hemba_male_figure1.jpg/255px-Hemba_male_figure1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Hemba_male_figure1.jpg/340px-Hemba_male_figure1.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hemba_male_figure1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hemba" title="Hemba">Hemba</a> male statue</div></div></div>
<p>The culture reflects the diversity of its hundreds of ethnic groups and their differing ways of life throughout the country—from the mouth of the River Congo on the coast, upriver through the rainforest and savanna in its centre, to the more densely populated mountains in the far east. Since the late 19th century, traditional ways of life have undergone changes brought about by colonialism, the struggle for independence, the stagnation of the Mobutu era, and most recently, the First and Second Congo Wars. Despite these pressures, the customs and cultures of the Congo have retained much of their individuality. The country's 81 million inhabitants (2016) are mainly rural. The 30% who live in urban areas have been the most open to <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western</a> influences.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The DRC has its influences on <a href="/wiki/Cuban_rumba" title="Cuban rumba">Cuban rumba</a>, originally kumba from Congo and <a href="/wiki/Merengue_music" title="Merengue music">merengue</a>. And those two later give birth to <a href="/wiki/Soukous" title="Soukous">soukous</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[233]</a></sup> Other African nations produce music genres derived from Congolese soukous. Some of the African bands sing in Lingala, one of the main languages in the DRC. The same Congolese soukous, under the guidance of "le sapeur", <a href="/wiki/Papa_Wemba" title="Papa Wemba">Papa Wemba</a>, have set the tone for a generation of young men always dressed up in expensive designer clothes. They came to be known as the fourth generation of Congolese music and mostly come from the former well-known band <a href="/wiki/Wenge_Musica" title="Wenge Musica">Wenge Musica</a>. 
The musical artist Elizo Kisonga, who now lives in England, is originally from Congo.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_(8756673901).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2074" data-file-width="3787" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_%288756673901%29.jpg/220px-Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_%288756673901%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_%288756673901%29.jpg/330px-Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_%288756673901%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_%288756673901%29.jpg/440px-Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_%288756673901%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stade_des_martyrs_0332_Kinshasa_(8756673901).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Stade_des_Martyrs" title="Stade des Martyrs">Stade des Martyrs</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Many sports are played in the DRC, including <a href="/wiki/Football_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Football in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">football</a>, basketball, and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Rugby union in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">rugby</a>. The sports are played in numerous stadiums throughout the country, including the <a href="/wiki/Stade_Frederic_Kibassa_Maliba" title="Stade Frederic Kibassa Maliba">Stade Frederic Kibassa Maliba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[234]</a></sup> As Zaire they participated in the World Cup Football (Final stage) in 1974.
</p><p>Internationally, the country is especially famous for its professional basketball <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a> and football players. <a href="/wiki/Dikembe_Mutombo" title="Dikembe Mutombo">Dikembe Mutombo</a> is one of the best African basketball players to ever play the game. Mutombo is well known for humanitarian projects in his home country. <a href="/wiki/Bismack_Biyombo" title="Bismack Biyombo">Bismack Biyombo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Eyenga" title="Christian Eyenga">Christian Eyenga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Kuminga" title="Jonathan Kuminga">Jonathan Kuminga</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Mudiay" title="Emmanuel Mudiay">Emmanuel Mudiay</a> are others who gained significant international attention in basketball. Several Congolese players and players of Congolese descent—including strikers <a href="/wiki/Romelu_Lukaku" title="Romelu Lukaku">Romelu Lukaku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yannick_Bolasie" title="Yannick Bolasie">Yannick Bolasie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dieumerci_Mbokani" title="Dieumerci Mbokani">Dieumerci Mbokani</a>—have gained prominence in world football. DR Congo has twice won the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Cup of Nations">African Cup of Nations</a> football tournament.
</p><p>DR Congo's women's national volleyball team lastly qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2021_Women%27s_African_Nations_Volleyball_Championship" title="2021 Women's African Nations Volleyball Championship">2021 Women's African Nations Volleyball Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[235]</a></sup> The country featured a national team in <a href="/wiki/Beach_volleyball" title="Beach volleyball">beach volleyball</a> that competed at the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%932020_CAVB_Beach_Volleyball_Continental_Cup" title="2018–2020 CAVB Beach Volleyball Continental Cup">2018–2020 CAVB Beach Volleyball Continental Cup</a> in both the women's and the men's section.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[236]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Media of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Media of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>
<p>Newspapers of the DRC include <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%27Avenir_(Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_newspaper)" title="L'Avenir (Democratic Republic of the Congo newspaper)">L'Avenir</a></i>, <i>Radion Télévision Mwangaza</i>, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=La_Conscience&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="La Conscience (page does not exist)">La Conscience</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Conscience" title="fr:La Conscience">fr</a>]</span></i>, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=L%27Observateur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="L'Observateur (page does not exist)">L'Observateur</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/L%27Observateur_(RDC)" title="fr:L'Observateur (RDC)">fr</a>]</span></i>, <i>Le Phare</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Potentiel" title="Le Potentiel">Le Potentiel</a></i>, <i>Le Soft</i> and <i>LeCongolais.CD</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[237]</a></sup> a web-based daily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[238]</a></sup> Radio Télévision Nationale Congolaise (RTNC) is the national broadcaster of the Democratic Republic of the Congo. RTNC currently broadcasts in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lingala_language" title="Lingala language">Lingala</a>, French, and English.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/List_of_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_writers" title="List of Democratic Republic of the Congo writers">Congolese authors</a> use literature as a way to develop a sense of <a href="/wiki/National_identity" title="National identity">national consciousness</a> amongst the people of the DRC. <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Kambemba_Yamusangie" title="Frederick Kambemba Yamusangie">Frederick Kambemba Yamusangie</a> writes literature for the between generations of those who grew up in the Congo, during the time when they were colonised, fighting for independence and after. Yamusangie in an interview<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[239]</a></sup> said he felt the distance in literature and wanted to remedy that he wrote the novel, Full Circle, which is a story of a boy named Emanuel who in the beginning of the book feels a difference in culture among the different groups in the Congo and elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[240]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%AFs_Neza_Boneza" title="Raïs Neza Boneza">Rais Neza Boneza</a>, an author from the Katanga province, wrote novels and poems to promote artistic expressions as a way to address and deal with conflicts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[241]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The term "Kikongo" in the Constitution  is actually referring to the Kituba language – which is known as <i>Kikongo ya leta</i> by its speakers – not the <a href="/wiki/Kongo_language" title="Kongo language">Kongo language</a> proper. The confusion arises from the fact that the government of the DRC officially recognizes and refers to the language simply as "Kikongo".</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-156"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-156">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The law on sexual violence, DRC 2006 (Les lois sur les violences sexuelles) reads (in French): <i>"Article 3, Paragraphe 7: De la mutilation sexuelle; Article 174g; Sera puni d’une peine de servitude pénale de deux à cinq ans et d’une amende de deux cent mille francs congolais constants, quiconque aura posé un acte qui porte atteinte à l’intégrité physique ou fonctionnelle des organes génitaux d’une personne. Lorsque la mutilation a entraîné la mort, la peine est de servitude pénale à perpétuité."</i><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140819085226/http://monusco.unmissions.org/LinkClick.aspx?fileticket=aXFfmf5vsm8%3D&amp;tabid=11245&amp;mid=14386&amp;language=en-US" rel="nofollow">"Les lois sur les violences sexuelles"</a> [The laws against sexual violence]. Archived from <a class="external text" href="http://monusco.unmissions.org/LinkClick.aspx?fileticket=aXFfmf5vsm8%3D&amp;tabid=11245&amp;mid=14386&amp;language=en-US" rel="nofollow">the original</a> on 19 August 2014<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">12 November</span> 2014</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Les+lois+sur+les+violences+sexuelles&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fmonusco.unmissions.org%2FLinkClick.aspx%3Ffileticket%3DaXFfmf5vsm8%253D%26tabid%3D11245%26mid%3D14386%26language%3Den-US&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADemocratic+Republic+of+the+Congo"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-169"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-169">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Coltan" title="Coltan">Coltan</a> is a major source of <a href="/wiki/Tantalum" title="Tantalum">tantalum</a> which is used in the fabrication of electronic components in computers and mobile phones. The coltan mines are small, and non-mechanized. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/africa/5209428.stm" rel="nofollow">DR Congo poll crucial for Africa"</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20101202153903/http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/africa/5209428.stm" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 2 December 2010 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>, BBC News. 16 November 2006.</span>
